The Murji'ah Argument from General Verses
Ghazali cites Murji'ah proof-texts and counters by redefining 'faith' as Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Murji'ah's use of general Quranic verses about reward does not prove that faith alone suffices, and how Ghazali counters by redefining 'faith' to include works.

Core Idea
General verses about reward do not automatically exclude works.

The Murji'ah school argued that faith alone, without works, guarantees salvation. They based this on Quranic verses that promise reward for believers in general terms. In this passage, Ghazali begins his refutation by showing that these verses actually refer to faith accompanied by works, i.e., Islam as a whole.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the verses Ghazali cites.
These are the verses the Murji'ah use as proof.
2
Identify the Murji'ah argument
The Murji'ah hold fast to the generalities of these verses. What do they conclude from them?
They conclude that faith alone is sufficient for reward.
3
Understand Ghazali's reinterpretation
Ghazali says 'faith' in these verses means faith with works, i.e., Islam. How does he justify this?
He refers to previous explanation that faith can be used to mean Islam.
4
Note the distinction
Distinguish between 'iman' (faith) and 'islam' (submission) in this context.
Islam includes heart, speech, and deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولقوله تعالى : ( وَاللَّهُ يُحِبُّ الْمُحْسِنِينَ ) (۱) وقال تعالى : ( إِنَّا لَا نُضِيعُ أَجْرَ مَنْ أَحْسَنَ عَمَلًا ) (٢) فهذه جملة من الآيات القرآنية الكريمة تمسك بعموماتها المرجئة . ولا حجة لهم في ذلك ، فإنه حيث ذكر الإيمان في هذه الآيات (۳) أريد به الإيمان مع العمل (٤) ، إذ بينا ان الإيمان قد يطلق ويراد به الإسلام ، وهو الموافقة بالقلب والقول والعمل . ودليل هذا التأويل (٥) أخبار كثيرة في معاقبة العاصين ومقادير العقاب (٦) ؛ وقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : يخرج من النار من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من إيمان . فكيف يخرج إذا لم يدخل (۷) . ومن القرآن ، قوله تعالى : إِنَّ اللهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَنْ يُشْرَكَ بِهِ وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَن يَشَاءُ ) (۸) والإستثناء بالمشيئة يدل على الإنقسام (۱) . وقوله تعالى : ( وَمَن يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ فَإِنَّ لَهُ نَارَ جَهَنَّمَ خَالِدِينَ فيها ) (۲) . وتخصيصه بالكفر تحكم . وقوله تعالى : ( ألا إِنَّ الظَّالِمِينَ فِي عذابٍ مُقِيمٍ ) (۳) وقال تعالى : ( وَمَن جَاءَ بِالسَّيِّئَةِ فَكُبَّتْ وُجُوهُهُمْ فِي النَّارِ ) (٤) فهذه العمومات في معارضة عموماتهم ، ولا بد من تسليط التخصيص والتأويل على الجانبين ، لأن الأخبار مصرحة بأن العصاة يعذبون (٦) ، بل قوله تعالى : ( وَإِن مِّنْكُمْ إِلَّا وَارِدُهَا ) (۷) كالصريح في أن ذلك لا بد منه للكل ، إذ لا يخلو مؤمن عن ذنب يرتكبه (۸)
And by His statement, the Exalted: 'And Allah loves the doers of good' (1), and He said, the Exalted: 'Indeed, We do not waste the reward of those who do good deeds' (2). So this is a collection of noble Quranic verses by whose generalities the Murji'ah hold fast. And there is no proof for them in that, for verily, when faith is mentioned in these verses (3), what is meant is faith with works (4), since we have explained that 'faith' may be used and what is meant is Islam, which is agreement with the heart, speech, and deeds. And the proof of this interpretation (5) is many reports about the punishment of sinners and the measures of punishment (6); and his statement, peace be upon him: 'There will come out from the Fire he who has in his heart the weight of a speck of faith.' So how can he come out if he did not enter (7)? And from the Quran is His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him, and He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' (8). And the exception by will indicates division (1). And His statement, the Exalted: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, then indeed for him is the Fire of Hell, abiding eternally therein' (2). And specifying it to disbelief is arbitrary. And His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, the wrongdoers are in an enduring punishment' (3). And He said, the Exalted: 'And whoever comes with an evil deed, their faces will be cast down into the Fire' (4). So these generalities are in opposition to their generalities, and it is necessary to apply specification and interpretation on both sides, because the reports explicitly state that sinners are punished (6). Rather, His statement, the Exalted: 'And there is not one of you but will come to it' (7) is almost explicit that this is inevitable for all, since there is no believer free from a sin he commits (8).
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Murji'ah position that faith alone (without works) is sufficient for salvation, using the general verses of the Quran. The author begins by citing two verses that the Murji'ah often cling to: 'And Allah loves the doers of good' and 'We do not waste the reward of those who do good deeds.' He then states that these verses are a collection by which the Murji'ah hold fast to their generalities. However, he immediately denies that these provide proof for them, explaining that when 'faith' is mentioned in these verses, it means faith accompanied by works (the Islamic concept of iman as inner conviction plus outer actions). He references a previous explanation that the term 'faith' can be used to mean 'Islam'—agreement of heart, speech, and deeds. This is the first layer of refutation: the verses are interpreted in a way that includes works. Next, he provides evidence for this interpretation: there are many reports about the punishment of sinners and the degrees of punishment, including the hadith that those with even a speck of faith will eventually exit Hell. The argument is that if such sinners never entered Hell, how could they exit? Then he cites the Quranic verse: 'Allah forgives not that partners be associated with Him, but forgives what is less than that for whom He wills.' The phrase 'for whom He wills' indicates a division—some are forgiven, some are not—implying that sinners can be punished. He then addresses another verse: 'Whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, indeed for him is the Fire of Hell, abiding eternally therein.' He notes that restricting this verse only to disbelief is arbitrary. Similarly, verses about 'wrongdoers' and 'those who come with an evil deed are cast into the Fire' are general. So these generalities (about punishment) stand in opposition to the generalities the Murji'ah use (about reward). It is necessary to apply specification and interpretation on both sides, because the reports explicitly affirm that sinners are punished. Finally, he cites the verse 'There is not one of you but will come to it (the Fire),' which is nearly explicit that everyone must pass over Hell (on the Sirat), and no believer is free from sin. Thus, the Murji'ah argument is countered by other clear texts.

Key Terms
الإيمان
الإسلام
المرجئة
العمومات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Murji'ah think that general verses about reward prove faith alone is sufficient.
Correction: Ghazali shows these verses refer to faith with works, not faith alone.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, when faith is mentioned in the verses cited, what is meant?
A) Faith alone
B) Faith plus works (Islam)
C) Only inner conviction
D) Only outward actions

Key Takeaway
The Murji'ah's proof verses actually refer to faith that includes works, not faith alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verses about Allah's love for 'doers of good,' do you automatically assume you are included, or do you let the verse expose your shortcomings? What specific good deed have you neglected this week that you now realize is part of 'faith' itself?
?
Are there areas of your life where you rely on general promises of Allah's mercy while ignoring the specific conditions attached? Name one sin you have justified to yourself thinking, 'Faith alone is enough' — how does Ghazali's argument challenge that comfort?
?
The Murji'ah took verses out of context to build a theology that required little of them. In what ways do you take Quranic verses out of context to avoid personal change? Will you commit to reading the full context of a verse you've been using as an excuse?

Evidence for Punishment from Hadith and Quran
Ghazali provides hadith and Quranic evidence for punishment of sinful believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key proofs Ghazali uses to show that believers who commit sins can be punished, including the hadith about exiting Hell and Quranic verses about punishment.

Core Idea
Believers can be punished for their sins; the hadith and Quran confirm this.

After establishing that the general verses about reward refer to faith with works, Ghazali now provides evidence that sinners among believers are indeed punished. He cites a well-known hadith and several Quranic verses that imply punishment for disobedience, even for believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the hadith and verses.
2
Analyze the hadith
The hadith says people with a speck of faith will exit Hell. What does that imply about entry?
It implies they entered Hell first.
3
Examine the Quranic verses
The verses about shirk forgiveness, disobedience, wrongdoers, and evil deeds. How do they support punishment?
They show that even believers may face punishment.
4
Understand the refutation
Ghazali refutes the Murji'ah by showing that these verses cannot be restricted only to disbelievers.
Specifying them to disbelief is arbitrary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولقوله تعالى : ( وَاللَّهُ يُحِبُّ الْمُحْسِنِينَ ) (۱) وقال تعالى : ( إِنَّا لَا نُضِيعُ أَجْرَ مَنْ أَحْسَنَ عَمَلًا ) (٢) فهذه جملة من الآيات القرآنية الكريمة تمسك بعموماتها المرجئة . ولا حجة لهم في ذلك ، فإنه حيث ذكر الإيمان في هذه الآيات (۳) أريد به الإيمان مع العمل (٤) ، إذ بينا ان الإيمان قد يطلق ويراد به الإسلام ، وهو الموافقة بالقلب والقول والعمل . ودليل هذا التأويل (٥) أخبار كثيرة في معاقبة العاصين ومقادير العقاب (٦) ؛ وقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : يخرج من النار من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من إيمان . فكيف يخرج إذا لم يدخل (۷) . ومن القرآن ، قوله تعالى : إِنَّ اللهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَنْ يُشْرَكَ بِهِ وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَن يَشَاءُ ) (۸) والإستثناء بالمشيئة يدل على الإنقسام (۱) . وقوله تعالى : ( وَمَن يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ فَإِنَّ لَهُ نَارَ جَهَنَّمَ خَالِدِينَ فيها ) (۲) . وتخصيصه بالكفر تحكم . وقوله تعالى : ( ألا إِنَّ الظَّالِمِينَ فِي عذابٍ مُقِيمٍ ) (۳) وقال تعالى : ( وَمَن جَاءَ بِالسَّيِّئَةِ فَكُبَّتْ وُجُوهُهُمْ فِي النَّارِ ) (٤) فهذه العمومات في معارضة عموماتهم ، ولا بد من تسليط التخصيص والتأويل على الجانبين ، لأن الأخبار مصرحة بأن العصاة يعذبون (٦) ، بل قوله تعالى : ( وَإِن مِّنْكُمْ إِلَّا وَارِدُهَا ) (۷) كالصريح في أن ذلك لا بد منه للكل ، إذ لا يخلو مؤمن عن ذنب يرتكبه (۸)
And by His statement, the Exalted: 'And Allah loves the doers of good' (1), and He said, the Exalted: 'Indeed, We do not waste the reward of those who do good deeds' (2). So this is a collection of noble Quranic verses by whose generalities the Murji'ah hold fast. And there is no proof for them in that, for verily, when faith is mentioned in these verses (3), what is meant is faith with works (4), since we have explained that 'faith' may be used and what is meant is Islam, which is agreement with the heart, speech, and deeds. And the proof of this interpretation (5) is many reports about the punishment of sinners and the measures of punishment (6); and his statement, peace be upon him: 'There will come out from the Fire he who has in his heart the weight of a speck of faith.' So how can he come out if he did not enter (7)? And from the Quran is His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him, and He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' (8). And the exception by will indicates division (1). And His statement, the Exalted: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, then indeed for him is the Fire of Hell, abiding eternally therein' (2). And specifying it to disbelief is arbitrary. And His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, the wrongdoers are in an enduring punishment' (3). And He said, the Exalted: 'And whoever comes with an evil deed, their faces will be cast down into the Fire' (4). So these generalities are in opposition to their generalities, and it is necessary to apply specification and interpretation on both sides, because the reports explicitly state that sinners are punished (6). Rather, His statement, the Exalted: 'And there is not one of you but will come to it' (7) is almost explicit that this is inevitable for all, since there is no believer free from a sin he commits (8).
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Murji'ah position that faith alone (without works) is sufficient for salvation, using the general verses of the Quran. The author begins by citing two verses that the Murji'ah often cling to: 'And Allah loves the doers of good' and 'We do not waste the reward of those who do good deeds.' He then states that these verses are a collection by which the Murji'ah hold fast to their generalities. However, he immediately denies that these provide proof for them, explaining that when 'faith' is mentioned in these verses, it means faith accompanied by works (the Islamic concept of iman as inner conviction plus outer actions). He references a previous explanation that the term 'faith' can be used to mean 'Islam'—agreement of heart, speech, and deeds. This is the first layer of refutation: the verses are interpreted in a way that includes works. Next, he provides evidence for this interpretation: there are many reports about the punishment of sinners and the degrees of punishment, including the hadith that those with even a speck of faith will eventually exit Hell. The argument is that if such sinners never entered Hell, how could they exit? Then he cites the Quranic verse: 'Allah forgives not that partners be associated with Him, but forgives what is less than that for whom He wills.' The phrase 'for whom He wills' indicates a division—some are forgiven, some are not—implying that sinners can be punished. He then addresses another verse: 'Whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, indeed for him is the Fire of Hell, abiding eternally therein.' He notes that restricting this verse only to disbelief is arbitrary. Similarly, verses about 'wrongdoers' and 'those who come with an evil deed are cast into the Fire' are general. So these generalities (about punishment) stand in opposition to the generalities the Murji'ah use (about reward). It is necessary to apply specification and interpretation on both sides, because the reports explicitly affirm that sinners are punished. Finally, he cites the verse 'There is not one of you but will come to it (the Fire),' which is nearly explicit that everyone must pass over Hell (on the Sirat), and no believer is free from sin. Thus, the Murji'ah argument is countered by other clear texts.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the verse about eternal fire only applies to disbelievers.
Correction: Ghazali says specifying it to disbelief is arbitrary; it applies to all disobedient.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith 'yukhriju min al-nar man kana fi qalbihi mithqal dharra min iman' imply?
A) Believers never enter Hell.
B) Believers can enter Hell but eventually exit.
C) Only disbelievers enter Hell.
D) Faith is enough to keep one out of Hell.

Key Takeaway
Both hadith and Quran show that believing sinners can be punished, contrary to the Murji'ah claim.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'He will come out of the Fire because of a speck of faith,' do you assume that your own faith qualifies you for that promise, or does it make you afraid of what might cause you to enter it in the first place? What is the weight of your faith measured against your disobedience?
?
If forgiveness of your lesser sins depends on 'whom He wills'—not on your mere avoidance of shirk—then what are you truly relying on for salvation? Does your daily life reflect trust in His mercy or presumption upon His pardon?
?
This passage forces you to accept that your disobedience, even as a believer, can lead to Hell. If you truly believed that tonight’s sin could land you in the Fire tomorrow, what would you change about your routine before you sleep tonight?

Balancing Generalities: The Necessity of Specification
Ghazali concludes by balancing general verses and citing universal passage through Fire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why both sets of general verses (reward and punishment) require specification and interpretation, and how this refutes the Murji'ah position.

Core Idea
Neither reward nor punishment verses can be taken absolutely; both need specification.

Having presented verses that threaten punishment, Ghazali now confronts the Murji'ah's generalities with opposing generalities. He argues that the only consistent approach is to apply specification (takhsis) and interpretation (ta'wil) to both sides. The conclusive proof is that even the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the Quran affirm that every soul will come to the Fire, meaning believers too.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the verses Ghazali introduces.
2
Understand the principle
Ghazali says both sets of generalities are in opposition. What must be done?
Specification and interpretation must be applied to both sides.
3
Examine the final proof
The verse 'There is not one of you but will come to it' supports universal accountability.
It implies everyone will face the Fire in some sense.
4
Connect to refutation
How does this dismantle the Murji'ah argument?
It shows that believers are not exempt from punishment; thus faith alone does not guarantee paradise without works.

The Necessary Specification of Punishment Verses and the Fate of Believers
Ghazali argues for the necessary specification of punishment verses and concludes that believers are not eternally punished.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why general punishment verses must be specified and interpreted, and how this leads to the conclusion that believers who die on tawhid are not eternally punished.

Core Idea
General punishment verses require specification to avoid contradiction; believers are not eternally punished.

Imam Ghazali addresses a critical theological question: do the Qur'anic verses that threaten eternal punishment apply to all sinners, including believers? In this passage, he argues that such general verses must be interpreted in light of other evidence, and he establishes the orthodox position that while disbelievers face eternal punishment, believers who die upon tawhid are ultimately saved, regardless of their sins.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement about exception by will
Understand that the exception 'illa ma sha'a Allah' indicates a division among sinners.
2
Examine the general punishment verses cited
Notice the verses that seem to promise eternal punishment for all disobedience.
3
Grasp the necessity of specification and interpretation
See why Ghazali insists these must be applied to both sides of apparently conflicting verses.
4
Discern the distinction between disbelief and lesser sins
Learn that shirk is unforgivable, but other sins may be forgiven, and the conclusion that monotheists are not eternally punished.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإستثناء بالمشيئة يدل على الإنقسام (۱) . وقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَمَن يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ فَإِنَّ لَهُ نَارَ جَهَنَّمَ خَالِدِينَ فيها ) (٢) . وتخصيصه بالكفر تحكم . وقوله تعالى : ( ألا إِنَّ الظَّالِمِينَ فِي عذابٍ مُقِيمٍ (٣) ﴾ وقال تعالى : ﴿ وَمَن جَاءَ بِالسَّيِّئَةِ فَكُبَّتْ وُجُوهُهُمْ فِي النَّارِ (٤) فهذه العمومات في معارضة عموماتهم ، ولا بد من تسليط التخصيص والتأويل على الجانبين ، لأن الأخبار مصرحة بأن العصاة يعذبون (٦) ، بل قوله تعالى : ( وَإِن مِّنْكُمْ إِلَّا وَارِدُهَا ) (۷) كالصريح في أن ذلك لا بد منه للكل ، إذ لا يخلو مؤمن عن ذنب يرتكبه(۸) من جحد نبوة الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم مثلا فهو كافر ، ولو لم يجعل مع الله إلها آخر ، والمغفرة منتفية عنه بلا خلاف . ويعفر ما دون الشرك تحت إمكان المغفرة ، فمن مات على التوحيد غير مخلد في النار وان ارتكب من الكبائر غير الشرط ما عساه أن يرتكب .
And the exception by the will indicates division. And His statement, the Exalted: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, then indeed for him is the Fire of Hell, abiding therein forever.' And specifying it to disbelief is arbitrary. And His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, the wrongdoers are in a lasting punishment.' And He said, the Exalted: 'And whoever comes with an evil deed, their faces will be thrown into the Fire.' So these general verses are in opposition to their general verses, and it is necessary to apply specification and interpretation to both sides, because the reports clearly state that sinners are punished. Rather, His statement, the Exalted: 'And there is none of you except that he will pass over it' is almost explicit that this is necessary for all, since no believer is free from a sin he commits. Whoever denies the prophethood of the Messenger, for example, is a disbeliever, even if he does not take another god with Allah, and forgiveness is excluded from him without dispute. And what is less than shirk falls under the possibility of forgiveness. So whoever dies upon tawhid will not be eternally in the Fire, even if he commits of the major sins besides shirk as much as he may commit.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument about the interpretation of verses threatening punishment for sin. The author begins by stating that the exception by the will indicates a division of sins into major and minor. He then cites several general verses warning of punishment for disobedience, wrongdoing, and evil deeds. These verses, he argues, stand in opposition to the general verses of the Mu'tazila that promise forgiveness. Therefore, both sets of verses must be subjected to specification (takhsīṣ) and interpretation (taʼwīl), because the reports clearly affirm that sinners will be punished. The key verse 'There is none of you except that he will pass over it' (Q. 19:71) is taken as nearly explicit that everyone must experience this passing, since no believer is sinless. The author then clarifies that one who denies prophethood is a disbeliever, even without shirk, and forgiveness is not for him. In contrast, sins less than shirk remain under the possibility of forgiveness. The conclusion: whoever dies upon tawḥīd will not be eternally in the Fire, even if they committed major sins other than shirk. This establishes the orthodox position that believers are not eternally punished.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'wa in minkum illā wāriduhā' means that everyone will enter Hellfire.
Correction: The verse refers to passing over the bridge (ṣirāṭ) above Hell, not entering it. Ghazali uses it to show that all people will experience this passing, not that they will be cast into the Fire.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the fate of someone who dies upon tawhid while having committed major sins other than shirk?
A) He will be eternally in the Fire.
B) He will not be eternally in the Fire.
C) His forgiveness is impossible.
D) He is considered a disbeliever.

Key Takeaway
Whoever dies upon tawhid will not be eternally in the Fire, even if they committed major sins other than shirk.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that major sins less than shirk are under the possibility of forgiveness. But are you relying on that possibility to continue sinning, or does it drive you to sincere repentance? What does your heart tell you about your own fate if you die tonight?
?
Ghazali says no believer is free from sin. Think of a sin you commit repeatedly. How does this lesson challenge you to both fear Allah’s punishment (even if temporary) and hope in His mercy, so that you actually change?
?
The verse 'wa in minkum illā wāriduhā' means everyone will pass over the Ṣirāṭ. Does the thought of that crossing, and the potential of entering the Fire even temporarily, stir you to reform now? What specific act will you change today because of this?

Proof that Believers Are Not Eternally Punished
Ghazali cites Quranic verses and hadith to argue that believers are not eternally punished for sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali uses Quranic verses and hadith to prove that a believer who commits major sins will not remain in Hell forever.

Core Idea
Eternal punishment for believers is not literal; other verses specify it away.

In this passage, Ghazali tackles a critical theological question: do believers who die in sin suffer eternal punishment? He begins by citing verses that seem to threaten everlasting fire, but then immediately shows how they are qualified by other divine texts. You will see how the Quran and hadith together preserve the hope of ultimate salvation for believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without translation. Let the rhythm and key terms (like 'إيمان', 'شرك', 'مشيئة') sink in.
The passage is dense with Quranic references.
2
Study the translation and commentary
Read the English translation and then the teacher commentary. Notice how Ghazali argues that general verses are 'specified' by other verses.
3
Analyze the specifying verses
Identify the verses that threaten eternal punishment and the verses that limit them (e.g., 4:48, the hadith about the mustard seed). Ask: what is the rule for interpreting such apparent contradictions?
This is the core of Ghazali's method.
4
Understand the implication
Reflect on the theological conclusion: no believer, no matter how sinful, will be eternally punished. How does this uphold both God's justice and mercy?

ثم قال : ﴿ ثُمَّ نُنَجِّي الَّذِينَ اتَّقَواْ ﴾
وقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَمَنَ يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ فَإِنَّ لَهُ نَارَ جَهَنَّمَ ﴾
وكل آية ذكر الله عز وجل العمل الصالح فيها مقروناً بالإيمان
وقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَمَن يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِنًا مُتَعَمِّداً فَجَزَاؤُهُ جَهَنَّمُ خَالِداً فِيهَا ﴾
وهذه العمومات أيضاً مخصوصة ، بدليل قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَنْ يَشَاءُ ﴾
فينبغي أن تبقى له مشيئة في مغفرة ما سوى الشرك
وكذلك قوله عليه السلام : « يخرج من النار من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من إيمان »
وقوله تعالى : ﴿ إِنَّا لا نُضِيعُ أَجْرَ مَنْ أَحْسَنَ عَمَلاً ﴾
وقوله تعالى : ﴿ إِنَّ اللَّهَ لا يُضِيعُ أَجْرَ الْمُحْسِنِينَ ﴾ فكيف يضيع أجر أصل الإيمان وجميع الطاعات بمعصية واحدة
وقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَمَنْ يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِناً مُتَعَمِّداً ﴾ أي لإيمانه وقد ورد على مثل هذا السبب
Then He said: "Then We save those who fear" and His saying: "And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, then indeed for him is the fire of Hell." And every verse in which Allah Almighty mentions righteous deeds coupled with faith. And His saying: "And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding therein." And these generalities are also specified, by the evidence of His saying: "And He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills." So it must be that He has will in forgiving what is other than shirk. Also His (peace be upon him) saying: "There will come out of the Fire whoever has in his heart a mustard seed's weight of faith." And His saying: "Indeed, We do not waste the reward of those who do good." And His saying: "Indeed, Allah does not waste the reward of the doers of good." So how could He waste the reward of the foundation of faith and all acts of obedience due to one sin? And His saying: "And whoever kills a believer intentionally" means on account of his faith, and it has been revealed on such an occasion.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the Quran and hadith that a believer who commits major sins is not eternally punished. Ghazali cites several verses that seem to threaten eternal punishment, but argues they are specified by other texts. He begins with verses about saving the God-fearing and threatening the disobedient. Then he mentions the verse about killing a believer intentionally, which seems to promise eternal Hell. He argues that these general verses are specified by the verse 'He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' (4:48), leaving room for God's will to forgive any sin less than shirk. He then cites the hadith about the mustard seed of faith ensuring eventual exit from Hell. He adds verses about God not wasting reward, arguing that it would be inconsistent to waste the reward of faith and all good deeds because of one sin. Finally, he interprets the verse about killing a believer as being revealed on a specific occasion (i.e., it refers to killing because of faith), thus it does not apply generally.

Key Terms
إيمان
عمل
تخليد
مشيئة
شرك
كبائر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verses threatening eternal punishment for sinners are taken literally without exception.
Correction: This passage shows they are specified by other texts; thus a believer who dies in sin is not eternally punished.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, why does the verse 'Whoever kills a believer intentionally' not imply eternal punishment for such a killer if he is a believer?
A) Because the killer is not a believer.
B) Because the verse was revealed concerning killing because of faith.
C) Because God always forgives murder.
D) Because the verse is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
A believer's sins do not negate the reward of faith; God's mercy and the intercession of faith ensure eventual salvation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you feel that all your good deeds are lost? Are you living under the weight of your failures rather than the hope of God's mercy? What would it take for you to truly believe that your faith matters more than your shortcomings?
?
Ghazali argues that the reward of faith and all acts of obedience cannot be wasted by one sin. Does your life reflect that conviction? What specific sin are you holding onto that contradicts this truth? How will you repent and trust that God's will to forgive includes you?
?
The hadith says that even a mustard seed of faith will eventually bring you out of Hell. Are you confident that you have that seed? What are you doing to nurture it? Or do you take it for granted? When you sin, do you immediately turn back to Allah, or do you despair?

Interpreting the Hadith on the Fornicator's Faith
Ghazali interprets the Prophetic hadith about the fornicator not being a believer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's interpretation of the hadith and how he distinguishes between the essence of faith and its perfection.

Core Idea
The fornicator is still a believer, but lacks perfect faith.

This lesson examines a key hadith often cited in debates about faith and sin. Ghazali shows that the Prophet's words do not mean the fornicator loses faith entirely, but rather that his faith is incomplete. He uses a powerful analogy to clarify the distinction between the reality of faith and its full perfection.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and translation
Read the Arabic hadith and its literal translation carefully. Notice the phrase 'while he is a believer'.
This hadith is often misunderstood.
2
Understand the Companions' view
Ghazali notes that the Companions did not adopt the Mu'tazilite doctrine that fornication removes one from faith. Recognize their position as a baseline.
3
Analyze the analogy
Ghazali compares the fornicator to an amputee. Reflect on why an amputee is said to be 'not a human' in a limited sense, yet still human. Connect this to faith.
The analogy is key to understanding Ghazali's point.
4
Apply the lesson
Consider how this interpretation affects the understanding of faith and major sins. Write down the distinction between essential faith and perfect faith.
This guards against extreme views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قال صلى الله عليه وسلم {ولا يزنى الزاني حين يزني وهو مؤمن} والصحابة رضي عنهم ما أعتقدوا مذهب المعتزلة في الخروج عن الإيمان بالزنا ولكن معناه غير مؤمن حقاً إيماناً تاماً كاملاً ، كما يقال للعاجز المقطوع الأطراف هذا ليس بإنسان اي ليس له الكمال الذي هو وراء حقيقة الإنسانية
And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'No fornicator fornicates while he is a believer.' And the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, did not adopt the Mu'tazilite doctrine of exiting from faith due to fornication. Rather, its meaning is that he is not truly a believer with complete and perfect faith, just as it is said of a disabled person with amputated limbs: 'This is not a human being,' meaning he does not have the perfection that goes beyond the reality of humanity.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a textual proof (from hadith) and its interpretation. Ghazali cites the well-known hadith that a fornicator does not commit fornication while being a believer. He then clarifies that the Companions did not understand this as the Mu'tazilites did—that committing a major sin like fornication removes one from the fold of faith entirely. Instead, the hadith means that the fornicator lacks the perfection of faith (iman tamm kamil), but his faith is still present. Ghazali uses the analogy of a person with amputated limbs who is still called a human being in the basic sense but is not called a complete human. Similarly, a sinful believer is still a believer in the foundational sense but not in the perfect sense. This guards against the Kharijite and Mu'tazilite view that major sins nullify faith.

Key Terms
الزنا (al-zina)
الإيمان التام (al-iman al-tamm)
الخروج عن الإيمان (al-khuruj ‘an al-iman)
المعتزلة (al-mu‘tazila)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith means that a fornicator is not a believer at all and loses all faith.
Correction: Ghazali explains that the hadith only negates perfect faith, not the essence of faith. The fornicator remains a believer in the basic sense, like an amputee is still human.

Checkpoint
How does Ghazali interpret the hadith 'No fornicator fornicates while he is a believer'?
A) The fornicator becomes a disbeliever.
B) The fornicator loses all faith.
C) The fornicator lacks perfect faith but still has the essence of faith.
D) The hadith is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali interprets the hadith to mean that a fornicator is a believer in the basic sense but lacks the perfection of faith, analogous to an amputee being called not a complete human.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever committed a major sin and felt your faith was completely gone? How does Ghazali's distinction between basic faith and perfect faith challenge or comfort you? What specific action will you take today to move from basic faith toward perfect faith?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim struggling with a major sin, do you tend to judge them as having no faith? How can you apply Ghazali's teaching to see them as a believer with imperfect faith, and what responsibility does that place on you to help them?
?
The analogy of the amputee human being: are you content with just the 'basic' faith that saves you from being a disbeliever, or are you striving for the perfection of faith that comes from obedience? What is one habit or sin you need to address to let your faith grow more complete?

Analogy of Faith as Head and Limbs
Analogy of iman to head and limbs, and interpretation of hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Ghazali's analogy of faith as a body where tasdiq is the head and acts of obedience are limbs, and how this analogy resolves the apparent conflict in the hadith about the adulterer.

Core Idea
In faith, inner conviction is the head; without it, there is no iman.

Imam Ghazali employs a vivid analogy from the human body to explain the structure of faith. He distinguishes between the essential core (tasdiq) and the supplementary acts. This lesson unpacks that analogy and shows how it answers a common question: does sin destroy faith?

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text once, then the translation. Notice the extended metaphor.
2
Identify the analogy
The head vs hands analogy is used for two things: being human and prayer. How does it apply to faith?
Tasdiq is the head, actions are limbs.
3
Analyze the hadith
Read the hadith and the author's explanation. Understand why the Mu'tazilite view is wrong.
The hadith means loss of perfect faith, not loss of faith.
4
Apply the analogy
Connect the analogy back to the hadith. How does the body analogy clarify the hadith?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرأس ، واليدان من الإنسان (۱) ، ومعلوم أنه يخرج عن كونه إنساناً بعدم الرأس (۲) ولا يخرج عنه بكونه مقطوع اليد (۳) وكذلك يقال للتسبيحات والتكبيرات من (٤) الصلاة ، وإن كانت لا تبطل بفقدها · فالتصديق بالقلب من الإيمان كالرأس من وجود الإنسان (٥) ، إذ ينعدم بعدمه وبقية الطاعات كالأطراف بعضها أعلى من بعض ، وقد قال صلى الله عليه وسلم { ولا يزنى الزاني حين يزني وهو مؤمن (٦) } الله والصحابة رضي عنهم ما أعتقدوا مذهب المعتزلة في الخروج عن الإيمان بالزنا )) ، ولكن معناه غير مؤمن حقاً إيماناً تاماً كاملاً ، كما يقال للعاجز المقطوع الأطراف هذا ليس بإنسان اي ليس له الكمال الذي هو وراء حقيقة الإنسانية (۸) (۱) أي من جملة أجزاء الإنسان · (۲) لأنه إذا ذهب الرأس ذهب الإنسان (۳) أو اليدين أو من أصل خلقته . (٤) التسبيحات التي يؤتى بها في الركوع والسجود ، والتكبيرات التي يؤتى بها عند الإفتتاح وعند كل رفع وخفض • (٥) أشار بذلك إلى أنه جزء من مفهومه (٦) الحديث متفق عليه من حديث أبي هريرة ، وفيه زيادة عندهما وهي : ولا يشرب الخمر حين يشربها وهو مؤمن ، ولا يسرق السارق حين يسرق وهو مؤمن ، ولا ينتهب نهبة ذات شرف يرفع الناس إليه فيها أبصارهم حين ينتهبها وهو مؤمن . وهكذا رواه أحمد والترمذي وإبن ماجه • (۷) وشرب الخمر والسرقة والإنتهاب والفل وإن وجد في بعض رواياته لفظ الخروج والنزع فهو على المبالغة والتشديد (۸) ومعناه : كامل الإيمان ومؤمن حقاً ، لأن حقيقة الإيمان كمال الخوف والورع إذ الأمة مجمعة أن -
The head and the two hands are from the human being (1), and it is known that he ceases to be a human being by the absence of the head (2), and he does not cease by being one whose hand is cut off (3). Similarly, it is said for the tasbihat and takbirat in prayer (4), even if the prayer is not invalidated by their absence. So affirmation (tasdiq) by the heart in faith is like the head in the existence of a human being (5), for faith ceases to exist with its absence, and the rest of acts of obedience are like limbs, some higher than others. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The adulterer does not commit adultery while he is a believer' (6). [Allah and the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) did not believe the Mu'tazilite doctrine of leaving faith by adultery], but its meaning is that he is not a true believer, a complete and perfect faith, just as it is said of the impotent one whose limbs are cut off: 'This is not a human being' — i.e., he does not have the perfection which is beyond the reality of humanity (8). (1) i.e., from the totality of parts of the human. (2) Because when the head goes, the human goes. (3) Or the two hands, or from the origin of his creation. (4) The tasbihat performed in bowing and prostration, and the takbirat performed at the beginning and at every raising and lowering. (5) He indicated by that that it is part of its concept. (6) The hadith is agreed upon from the hadith of Abu Huraira, and there is an addition in both: 'And the wine drinker does not drink wine while he is a believer, and the thief does not steal while he is a believer, and the plunderer does not plunder a valuable thing towards which people raise their eyes while he is plundering and he is a believer.' It is also narrated by Ahmad, al-Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah. (7) And drinking wine, stealing, plundering, and the like — even if the wording of 'leaving' and 'removal' occurs in some of its narrations, it is for hyperbole and emphasis. (8) And its meaning: complete faith and truly a believer, because the reality of faith is the perfection of fear and piety, for the community is agreed that —
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory analogy and a defense of a sound understanding of a prophetic hadith. The author begins by using the example of the human body: the head and hands are parts of a human, but the absence of the head negates humanness entirely, while the absence of hands does not. He then applies this to prayer: the optional formulas of glorification (tasbihat) and magnification (takbirat) are from prayer, but their loss does not invalidate it. The key point comes next: affirmation (tasdiq) by the heart is to faith as the head is to the human. Without tasdiq, there is no iman; with it, other acts of obedience become like limbs, some of which are higher in rank than others. The author then cites the famous hadith: 'The adulterer does not commit adultery while he is a believer.' He clarifies that the early community (the Companions) did not accept the Mu'tazilite view that such a sin expels one entirely from iman. Rather, the hadith means that the person is not a true, complete, and perfect believer at that moment. The analogy of the disabled person whose limbs are cut off is used: we say 'this is not a human' meaning he lacks the perfection of a complete human, not that he is no longer a human being. The footnotes reinforce these points: tasdiq is an integral part of the concept of iman, the hadith is sound and has additional wording about wine-drinking, theft, and plunder, and the wording of 'leaving' or 'removal' in some versions is hyperbolic and emphatic, not literal. The last footnote explains that the reality of iman is the perfection of fear and piety, but it cuts off at the page break, implying the community is agreed on this understanding.

Key Terms
التصديق
الإيمان
الرأس
الأطراف
الزنا
المعتزلة
الخوف
الورع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'The adulterer does not commit adultery while he is a believer' means that the person becomes a complete disbeliever (as Mu'tazilites claim).
Correction: Ghazali explains that it means loss of perfect faith, not loss of faith entirely. Just as a person missing limbs is still human but imperfect, a sinner is still a believer but imperfect in faith.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Ghazali's analogy, what does the head represent in relation to faith?
A) The good deeds like prayer and fasting
B) The affirmation of the heart (tasdiq)
C) The avoidance of major sins
D) The fear of Allah

Key Takeaway
Faith is essentially heart affirmation; acts complete it but sin does not erase it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you quickly tell yourself that your faith is still perfect, or do you feel the gap between your affirmation of Allah and your actions? How does this analogy force you to re-examine your own faith?
?
If tasdiq is the head of iman, without which faith ceases, then ask yourself today: is your heart truly affirming Allah's commands even when you fail to act? Or have you let actions become the substitute for conviction?
?
The hadith says the adulterer is not a believer while sinning. Consider a sin you struggle with. Will you allow yourself to think you are still a perfect believer in that moment? Or will you accept your imperfection and strive to restore the completeness of your iman?

Increase and Decrease of Faith: Objection and Answer
Reply to objection that iman increases/decreases if tasdiq is its essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ghazali reconciles the Salaf's statement that faith increases and decreases with his view that faith is essentially tasdiq (affirmation).

Core Idea
Faith increases in actions, not in its essence.

A common objection against the view that faith is essentially affirmation (tasdiq) is that the Salaf unanimously held that faith increases and decreases. If faith is a simple affirmation, how can it change? In this passage, Imam Ghazali defends the Salaf's statement while preserving the definition of faith as tasdiq. He argues that the increase and decrease refer to actions, which are not part of faith's essence but additional to it.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The passage begins with an objection: the Salaf said faith increases by obedience and decreases by disobedience, but if faith is tasdiq, increase and decrease are impossible. Consider the force of this objection before reading the answer.
2
Understand the authority of the Salaf
Ghazali affirms the Salaf as 'upright witnesses' whose statement cannot be rejected. He does not disagree with them but seeks to understand their words correctly.
3
Analyze the argument that actions are not part of faith's essence
Ghazali argues that the Salaf's statement itself proves that actions are not part of faith's essence or constitutive pillars; they are additional. Faith (tasdiq) does not increase in itself; it is the actions that increase.
4
Reflect on the analogy of the head and beard
The analogy clarifies: a person does not increase by his head (essential part) but by his beard and appearance (non-essential). Similarly, faith does not increase in its essence but through actions.
5
Examine the treatment of major sins
Ghazali explains that major sinners do not become disbelievers; they lose the 'reality' of faith (fear and piety) but retain the 'name' (tasdiq and adherence). A subtle point about modesty is added.
This shows how increase/decrease in actions affects the quality of faith, not its essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : فإن قلت . فقد إتفق السلف على أن الإيمان يزيد وينقص ، یزید بالطاعة وينقص بالمعصية ، فإذا كان (۱) التصديق هو الإيمان فلا يتصور فيه زيادة ولا نقصان (۳) فأقول . السلف هم الشهود العدول (۲) وما لأحد عن قولهم عدول (٤) فما ذكروه حق ، وإنما الشأن في فهمه ، وفيه دليل على أن العمل ليس من أجزاء الإيمان (٥) ، وأركان وجوده ، (٥) ، وأركان وجوده ، بل هو مزيد عليه يزيد به والزائد موجود ، والناقص موجود ، والشيء لا يزيد بذاته ، فلا يجوز أن يقال الإنسان يزيد برأسه ، بل يقال : يزيد بلحيته وسمته ، ولا يجوز أن يقال : الصلاة تزيد أهل الكبائر ليسوا بكافرين ، وإذا فسق بالزنا وشرب الخمر خرج من حقيقة الإيمان وهو الخوف والورع، ولم يخرج من اسمه وهو التصديق والتزام الشريعة ، وفيه معنى لطيف كأنه يرتفع عنه إيمان الحياء لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : «الحياء من الإيمان ، والمستحي لا يكشف عورته على حرام ، ويبقى إيمان الإسلام والتوحيد وإيجاب الأحكام » . (۱) وفي نسخة أخرى : فإن كان التصديق . الخ والإيمان هو التصديق ولا يتزايد في نفسه . (٢) أي لا يزيد بإنضمام الطاعات إليه ، ولا ينقص بإرتكاب المعاصي ، إذ التصديق في الحالين على ما قبلهما ؛ وهذا مخالف لما ذهب إليه السلف فكيف التطبيق بين القولين ؛ (۳) لأخبار وردت في ذلك منها : خير القرون قرني ، ثم الذين يلونهم ، وقد أثنى عليهم الله سبحانه في مواضع من كتابه العزيز ، منها قوله : «رضي الله عنهم ورضوا عنه ) ومنها : وأتبعوهم بإحسان (٤) عن قولهم الذين قالوه ورأيهم الذي رأوه ، عدول أصلاً (٥) التي تتركب منها ماهيته ، وأركان وجوده بحيث لا يوجد ولا يتحقق إلا به كما هو شأن الركنية
Issue: If you say: The Salaf agreed that faith increases and decreases; it increases by obedience and decreases by disobedience. If (1) affirmation (tasdiq) is faith, then increase and decrease are inconceivable in it (3). I say: The Salaf are the upright witnesses (2), and no one can deviate from their statement (4). What they mentioned is true, but the matter lies in understanding it. It is evidence that action is not part of the components of faith (5) and pillars of its existence, but rather it is additional to it; faith increases by it. The thing that increases exists, and the thing that decreases exists, and a thing does not increase in its essence. So it is not permissible to say that a human increases by his head, but rather one says: he increases by his beard and his good appearance. And it is not permissible to say: prayer increases... The people of major sins are not disbelievers. When one commits fornication or drinks wine, he leaves the reality of faith, which is fear and piety, but he does not leave its name, which is affirmation (tasdiq) and adherence to the sharia. There is a subtle meaning here: it is as if the faith of modesty is removed from him, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Modesty is from faith,' and the modest person does not uncover his private parts for what is forbidden, and the faith of Islam, tawhid, and the obligation of rulings remain. (1) In another copy: 'If affirmation is...' etc., and faith is affirmation and does not increase in itself. (2) Meaning: it does not increase by the addition of acts, nor does it decrease by committing sins, because affirmation is in both cases as it was before; and this is contrary to what the Salaf held, so how is the reconciliation between the two sayings? (3) Due to reports that have come concerning that, among them: 'The best of generations is my generation, then those who follow them,' and Allah praised them in places of His noble Book, including His saying: 'Allah is pleased with them and they are pleased with Him' and including: 'and those who follow them in goodness.' (4) From their statement which they said and their opinion which they held, as a definitive deviation. (5) Which the essence is composed of, and the pillars of its existence, such that it does not exist nor is it realized except with it, as is the matter of being a pillar.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer about the nature of faith, specifically whether it can increase and decrease. The objection states that the Salaf unanimously held that iman increases with obedience and decreases with sin; but if tasdiq (affirmation) is the essence of iman, it cannot increase or decrease because one either affirms or not. The author begins his answer by affirming the Salaf's authority: they are upright witnesses whose statement cannot be rejected. He then explains that the Salaf's statement itself is evidence that actions are not part of the essence or constitutive pillars of iman; rather, actions are something additional. Faith (i.e., tasdiq) itself does not increase or decrease; it is the actions that increase or decrease, and they are additional to the essence. He uses an analogy: a person does not increase in his head (the essential part), but increases in his beard and good appearance (non-essential additions). Similarly, prayer does not increase... (the text trails off). He then addresses the status of major sinners: they are not disbelievers. When one commits adultery or drinks wine, he leaves the reality of iman which is fear and piety, but he does not leave its name, which is tasdiq and commitment to the sharia. A subtle point: such a person loses the 'iman of modesty' because modesty is from faith, and a modest person would not commit such acts; yet he retains the iman of Islam, tawhid, and obligation of rulings. The footnotes provide additional clarifications: one variant reads 'If affirmation is faith...', and explains that tasdiq does not increase or decrease; the Salaf's sayings about increase are understood as increase in fear and piety, not in the essence of tasdiq. The reports praising the early generations are cited to support their authority. The footnotes also explain that 'pillars' means that without which the thing does not exist.

الزيادة والنقصان
التصديق
العمل

الورع
الحياء

Correction: Ghazali shows that the increase and decrease refer to actions, not to the essence of tasdiq. The Salaf's statement is true and consistent with tasdiq being the essence.

Key Takeaway
Imam Ghazali upholds the Salaf's statement by distinguishing between the essence of faith (tasdiq) and its increase through actions; actions are additional and can vary without affecting the core affirmation.

Iman's Increase and Decrease: The Salaf's Statement Explained
Ghazali answers an objection about iman increasing and decreasing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ghazali reconciles the Salaf's statement that iman increases and decreases with his definition of iman as tasdiq (verification of the heart).

Core Idea
Iman increases and decreases, but never in its essence.

Imam al-Ghazali now addresses a critical objection: if iman is simply tasdiq (verification of the heart), how can it increase or decrease as the Salaf said? The answer lies in distinguishing the essence of iman from its accompanying actions. In this passage, Ghazali defends the Salaf's statement while preserving the integrity of his definition.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the first part of the passage where the objector states the Salaf's position and the apparent contradiction with tasdiq.
Note that the objector sees increase and decrease as impossible for a single, indivisible mental state.
2
Understand Ghazali's defense
Ghazali affirms the Salaf's statement as true but insists on correct understanding. He points out that the statement itself proves actions are not part of iman's essence.
He calls the Salaf 'upright witnesses'—their word is not to be rejected.
3
Analyze the head-and-beard analogy
The analogy shows that a thing does not increase by its essence (the head) but by external additions (the beard). Apply this to iman: actions are external additions.
The head is part of the man, but his increase is by the beard, which is not part of his essence.
4
Analyze the prayer analogy
Prayer's essence is its obligatory acts (ruku', sujud); increase comes from the sunan (supererogatory elements), not from the essential pillars.
This reinforces that increase is in associated virtues, not the core.
5
Conclude the lesson
Iman has a real existence (tasdiq) and after that existence it varies in strength through actions, but the essence of tasdiq itself is fixed.
This preserves both the Salaf's statement and the definition of iman as tasdiq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : فإن قلت . فقد إتفق السلف على أن الإيمان يزيد وينقص ، یزید بالطاعة وينقص بالمعصية ، فإذا كان (۱) التصديق هو الإيمان فلا يتصور فيه زيادة ولا نقصان (۳) فأقول . السلف هم الشهود العدول (۲) وما لأحد عن قولهم عدول (٤) فما ذكروه حق ، وإنما الشأن في فهمه ، وفيه دليل على أن العمل ليس من أجزاء الإيمان (٥) ، وأركان وجوده ، بل هو مزيد عليه يزيد به والزائد موجود ، والناقص موجود ، والشيء لا يزيد بذاته ، فلا يجوز أن يقال الإنسان يزيد برأسه ، بل يقال : يزيد بلحيته وسمته ، ولا يجوز أن يقال : الصلاة تزيد بالركوع والسجود (٦) ، بل تزيد بالآداب والسنن (۲) فهذا تصريح بإن الإيمان له وجود ، ثم بعد الوجود يختلف حاله بالزيادة والنقصان
Issue: For you say: The Salaf agreed that iman increases and decreases, increases by obedience and decreases by disobedience. So if (1) tasdiq (verification) is iman, then increase and decrease cannot be conceived in it (3). So I say: The Salaf are the upright witnesses (2) and no one has a turning away from their statement (4). What they mention is true, but the matter lies in understanding it. In it is evidence that action is not a part of iman (5) nor a pillar of its existence; rather it is additional to it, and the iman increases by it. The increasing thing exists, the decreasing thing exists, and a thing does not increase by itself. So it is not permissible to say a man increases by his head, but it is said: he increases by his beard and his character. Nor is it permissible to say prayer increases by bowing and prostration (6), but rather it increases by etiquettes and sunan (2). So this is a declaration that iman has existence, then after existence its state differs by increase and decrease.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer structure. The objector argues: The Salaf said iman increases and decreases, but if iman is tasdiq (verification by the heart), it cannot increase or decrease because it is a single mental state. Ghazali responds: The Salaf are trustworthy and their statement is true, but it requires correct interpretation. He explains that their statement actually proves that actions are not part of the essence of iman; rather they are external additions that accompany iman. Just as a man does not increase by his head (which is part of him) but by his beard and character (which are external), so iman does not increase in itself but by the actions that are added to it. Similarly, the essential parts of prayer (ruku' and sujud) do not increase the prayer's essence; rather, the prayer increases through the etiquettes and sunan attached to it. Thus, iman has a real existence (tasdiq), and after that existence, it can vary in strength through its associated works. Ghazali does not deny increase and decrease but redefines them as changes in accompanying factors, not in the essence of tasdiq itself. The parenthetical numbers refer to glosses that explain or expand on the text, but the main argument is clear.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ghazali denies that iman can increase or decrease at all.
Correction: Ghazali affirms increase and decrease but locates the change in the accompanying actions, not in the essence of tasdiq.

Checkpoint

B) That actions are not part of iman and are only external additions.
C) That tasdiq can increase and decrease like a quantity.

Key Takeaway
Iman (tasdiq) has a fixed essence but varies in strength through the actions that accompany it.

?

Iman as a Shared Name: The First Aspect
Ghazali answers the puzzle of tasdiq being one by classifying iman as a shared name

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali calls iman a shared name (ism mushtarak) and how the first aspect resolves the puzzle of tasdiq being single yet iman increasing and decreasing.

Core Idea
Iman is a shared name; its first meaning is simple belief of the common people.

Ghazali addresses a lingering puzzle: if tasdiq (heartfelt affirmation) is a single characteristic, how can it increase or decrease? He cuts through the confusion by introducing a key classification: iman is a shared name applied in three different senses. In this lesson, we explore the first and most basic sense, which explains why the iman of the common people is a simple affirmation without deeper realization.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the puzzle
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the objector asks how tasdiq, being one thing, can increase or decrease. This is the puzzle that Ghazali resolves.
The parenthetical numbers are likely cross-references from the original text; ignore them for now.
2
Understand Ghazali's answer: iman is a shared name
Ghazali says he will drop evasion and uncover the truth. He declares that 'iman' is a shared name (ism mushtarak) applied in three aspects. This means the term has multiple distinct meanings, not a single one.
A shared name resolves the puzzle because increase and decrease can refer to different meanings, not the same one.
3
Focus on the first aspect
The first aspect is tasdiq by the heart through belief and imitation, without unveiling or expansion of the chest. This is the iman of the common people and nearly all creation except the elite. Understand that this level is basic and does not involve deep spiritual realization.
The elite (khawass) have a higher form of iman that includes kashf (unveiling).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت فالأشكال قائم في أن التصديق كيف يزيد وينقص وهو خصلة واحدة (٤) ؟ فأقول : إذا تركنا المداهنة ولم نكترث بتشغيب من تشغب وكشفنا الغطاء إرتفع الإشكال فنقول : الإيمان إسم مشترك يطلق من ثلاثة أوجه (٠) الأول - أنه يطلق للتصديق بالقلب على سبيل الإعتقاد والتقليد من غير كشف وإنشراح صدر ، وهو إيمان العوام (٦): بل إيمان الخلق كلهم إلا الخواص (۷)
For you say: The puzzle remains as to how tasdiq increases and decreases while it is a single characteristic (4)? So I say: When we abandon flattery and pay no heed to the agitation of those who stir up trouble, and we remove the veil, the puzzle is resolved. So we say: Iman is a shared name applied from three aspects (0). The first: that it is applied for tasdiq by the heart by way of belief and imitation without unveiling and expansion of the chest; it is the iman of the common people (6): rather, the iman of all creation except the elite (7).
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is another objection-and-answer. The objector persists: How can tasdiq (which is a single characteristic) increase or decrease? Ghazali responds by dropping rhetorical evasion and uncovering the truth. He introduces a key conceptual tool: 'iman' is a shared name (ism mushtarak) — a term with multiple distinct meanings. It is applied from three aspects. He then explains the first aspect: iman as mere tasdiq by the heart through belief and imitation (taqlid), without spiritual unveiling (kashf) or expansion of the chest. This is the iman of the common people ('awamm). He even says it is the iman of all creation except the elite (khawass). This establishes that the iman of the general public is a simple affirmation without deep spiritual realization. The increase and decrease of iman is then understood not as a change in this basic tasdiq but as a shift between different levels or aspects of iman. The parenthetical notes likely elaborate on who the elite are, but the main point is that iman is a term with multiple senses, resolving the logical puzzle.

The First Meaning of Iman: Conviction That Increases and Decreases
Ghazali answers the objection by defining iman as a shared name and elaborates on its first sense as a variable conviction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali resolves the objection that tasdiq cannot increase by showing that iman is a shared name and its first meaning—taqlidi conviction—admits strength and weakness.

Core Idea
Iman is not a single simple quality; even in its basic sense, conviction can be tight or loose.

Ghazali addresses a common objection: if iman is simply tasdiq (affirmation), how can it increase? He cuts through the confusion by clarifying that the term 'iman' is used in multiple senses. In this lesson, we explore the first sense—the faith of the common people—which is a conviction that can strengthen or weaken.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and Ghazali's response
Read the passage from 'فإن قلت' to 'ارتفع الإشكال'. Notice the objector's assumption that tasdiq is a single characteristic, and Ghazali's strategy of dismissing obstruction.
Ghazali sets aside debate and declares the term is shared.
2
Understand the first definition of iman
Read the definition: 'الإيمان اسم مشترك... وهو إيمان العوام'. Grasp that the first meaning is tasdiq based on imitation, without inner illumination.
This includes most people, even some scholars.
3
Analyze the knot analogy and evidence
Read the analogy of the knot and the examples of Jews and Christians. Then read the Quranic verses. Understand how deeds affect the strength of conviction.
The knot can tighten or loosen; deeds increase faith like water for trees.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت فالأشكال قائم في أن التصديق كيف يزيد وينقص وهو خصلة واحدة (٤) ؟
فأقول : إذا تركنا المداهنة ولم نكترث بتشغيب من تشبث الغطاء إرتفع الإشكال
فنقول : الإيمان إسم مشترك يطلق من ثلاثة أوجه (0)
وكشفنا الأول - أنه يطلق للتصديق بالقلب على سبيل الإعتقاد والتقليد من غير كشف وإنشراح صدر ، وهو إيمان العوام (٦): بل إيمان الخلق كلهم إلا الخواص (۷)
(٤) والخصلة بالضم الحالة والخصلة يشير إلى أنه بسيط وبساطته تقتضي عدم قبوله الزيادة والنقص
(0) وأصل الشغب : تهييج الشر ، يقال : شغب القوم ، وعليهم وبهم شغباً من باب نفع ضد الخواص
(٦) جمع وهم فاضرب على ذلك
(۷) الخلق كلهم : فدخل فيهم المشتغلون بالعلوم الظاهرة ، ممن لم يكشف لهم من أسرار الحق شيء فهم كذلك بمنزلة العوام وإيمانهم كإيمانهم بل ربما أن بعض السوقة إذا ألقى إليه شيء من خواص الإيمان يتلقاه بالإقبال عليه، وهؤلاء بمعزل عنه لما نشأ في طباعهم من تحصيل علومهم العجب والحسد والكبر ، وسائر المذام فلا يستقر في قلبه ما يلقي إليه حسبما ألفه من طبعه من مناقضة ، ومنع ورد وأبطال
وهذا الإعتقاد عقدة (۱) على القلب ، تارة تشتد وتقوى ، وتارة تضعف وتسترخي (1) ، كالعقدة على الخيط مثلا ، ولا تستبعد هذا واعتبره باليهودي وصلابته في عقيدته التي لا يمكن نزوعه عنها بتخويف وتحذير ، ولا بتخييل (۲) ووعظ ، ولا بتحقيق وبرهان
وكذلك النصراني والمبتدعة (۳) وفيهم من يمكن تشکیکه بادنی کلام، ويمكن استنزاله عن إعتقاده بأدنى استمالة أو تخويف مع أنه غير شاك في عقده (٤) كالأول ولكنهما متفاوتان في شدة التصميم (٥) وهذا موجود في الإعتقاد الحق أيضاً والعمل يؤثر في نماء هذا التصميم وزيادته ، كما يؤثر سقي الماء في نماء الأشجار ولذلك قال تعالى : فَزَادَتْهُمْ إِيمَاناً (٦) وقال تعالى : ﴿لِيَزْدَادُواْ إِيمَاناً مَّعَ إِيمَانِهِمْ﴾ (۷) هذا بالنسبة للخلق كلهم ، أما الخواص من الناس المستثنون من هؤلاء وهم الذين أفاض الله على قلوبهم بأنوار المعارف وحلاهم بحلية الوقار والسكينة ، وأنعم عليهم بأنواع اللطائف
If you say: the problem remains: how does tasdiq (affirmation) increase and decrease while it is a single characteristic (khislah)? I say: if we abandon flattery and disregard the obstruction of whoever obstructs, the problem is removed. So we say: iman (faith) is a shared name (ism mushtarak), applied from three aspects. And we have uncovered the first: it is applied to tasdiq in the heart on the basis of belief (i'tiqad) and imitation (taqlid) without inner uncovering (kashf) and expansion of the breast, and that is the iman of the common people (al-awamm); rather, the iman of all creatures except the elite (al-khawass). (Footnote 4: 'khislah' with dammah means state/characteristic; he points out that it is simple, and its simplicity necessitates that it does not admit increase and decrease. 0: the root of 'shaghba' is incitement of evil. 6: they are a multitude, so strike that out. 7: all creatures: includes those occupied with external sciences, from whom nothing of the secrets of truth has been uncovered; they are like the common people, indeed some of the common people may receive something of the special characteristics of iman with acceptance, while these are remote from it due to the habit they have developed of pride, envy, and arrogance in their sciences, so what is presented to them does not settle in their hearts as it should, due to their habit of contradiction, rejection, and nullification.) This belief is a knot on the heart, sometimes tightening and strengthening, sometimes weakening and relaxing, like a knot on a thread, for example. Do not consider this far-fetched; consider the Jew and his firmness in his belief, which he cannot be made to abandon by intimidation, warning, imagination, preaching, verification, or proof. Likewise the Christian and the innovators (mubtadi'a); among them are those who can be unsettled by the slightest speech and can be led away from their belief by the slightest inducement or intimidation, even though he is not doubting in his knot like the first, yet they differ in intensity of determination. This also exists in true belief. Action affects the growth of this determination and its increase, just as watering affects the growth of trees. Therefore, the Exalted said: 'so it increased them in faith' (Q 9:124), and the Exalted said: 'that they may increase in faith upon their faith' (Q 48:4). This is concerning all creatures. As for the elite of people, those excluded from these, they are those upon whose hearts God has poured the lights of divine knowledge, adorned them with the adornment of dignity and tranquility, and bestowed upon them various graces.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer followed by a definition and its elaboration. The objector argues: if tasdiq (affirmation of the heart) is a simple single quality, how can it increase and decrease? Ghazali responds by first setting aside stubborn debate, then declaring that the term 'iman' is not univocal; it is a shared name (ism mushtarak) applied in three senses. He then unveils the first sense: it is the heart's affirmation based on belief (i'tiqad) and imitation (taqlid) without inner illumination or expansion (kashf wa inshirah). This is the faith of the common people (al-awamm) — indeed of all people except the elect elite (al-khawass). He defends this by explaining that even among those who claim knowledge, many lack the inner opening and thus are like the commoners. He then likens this conviction to a knot on the heart; it can be tight or loose, as observed in the Jew or Christian whose conviction may be immovable or easily shaken. Hence, true or false belief can vary in strength. Good deeds (a'mal) strengthen this determination, as watering strengthens trees. He cites Quranic verses (9:124, 48:4) that explicitly mention increase of faith. Finally, he distinguishes the elite (al-khawass), who have been illuminated by divine secrets, as a special class; their faith is not merely this first type. Thus the passage establishes that faith admits degrees in its first and most common meaning, and the term itself has multiple references.

Key Terms
إيمان
تصديق
تقليد
عوام
خواص
عقدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tasdiq is a simple indivisible quality that cannot increase or decrease.
Correction: The term 'iman' is applied in multiple senses; even in the first sense, conviction can vary in strength like a knot that tightens or loosens.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what is the first meaning of 'iman' as a shared name?
A) Heart's affirmation with inner expansion and insight
B) Heart's affirmation on the basis of belief and imitation without inner uncovering
C) The faith of the elite only
D) A single knot that never changes

Key Takeaway
Iman in its first sense is a conviction based on imitation that can strengthen or weaken, and it increases through righteous deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine your own heart, is your conviction like a tight knot or a loose one? What daily deeds are you doing to water that knot and make it stronger?
?
You may have inherited your faith through imitation (taqlid). Are you content with that, or are you actively seeking the inner illumination that distinguishes the elite?
?
If your faith truly increased with every good deed, would your actions today reflect that belief—or are you neglecting deeds that could tighten your conviction?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
6 min
Faith as a Knot on the Heart: Strength, Weakness, and Increase by Actions
Ghazali explains faith as a knot that strengthens with actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's analogy of faith as a knot that varies in strength and how actions influence its increase.

Core Idea
Faith is a knot on the heart that strengthens with actions, like a tree growing with water.

Imam al-Ghazali opens this passage with a vivid analogy: belief is like a knot tied on the heart. Some knots are firm and unshakable, while others are loose and easily undone. He then argues that actions—especially acts of obedience—serve to tighten this knot, increasing the determination and certainty of faith. This lesson will unpack that analogy and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully

Notice the repetition of key terms like 'uqdah' (knot) and 'tasmeem' (determination).
2
Identify the central analogy
Identify what the 'knot' represents and how its strength varies. Pay attention to the examples of the Jew, Christian, and innovators.
The knot is belief (i'tiqad) itself—its firmness differs among people.

Find where Ghazali states that actions influence the growth of this determination. Note the Quranic verses he cites and the analogy of watering a tree.
The verses are 9:124 and 48:4.

Consider how your own acts of worship or daily actions affect your inner certainty. Ghazali invites you to observe your own heart during times of devotion and laxity.
This connects the lesson to your own spiritual practice.
