⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا الإعتقاد عقدة على القلب، تارة تشتد وتقوى، وتارة تضعف وتسترخي، ولا تستبعد هذا واعتبره باليهودي وصلابته في عقيدته التي لا يمكن نزوعه عنها بتخويف وتحذير، ولا بتخييل ووعظ، ولا بتحقيق وبرهان، وكذلك النصراني والمبتدعة وفيهم من يمكن تشکیکه بادنی كلام، ويمكن استنزاله عن إعتقاده بأدنى استمالة أو تخويف مع أنه غير شاك في عقده كالأول ولكنهما متفاوتان في شدة التصميم، وهذا موجود في الإعتقاد الحق أيضاً والعمل يؤثر في نماء هذا التصميم وزيادته، كما يؤثر سقي الماء في نماء الأشجار، ولذلك قال تعالى: فَزَادَتْهُمْ إِيمَاناً، وقال تعالى: لِيَزْدَادُوا إِيمَاناً مَعَ إِيمَانِهِمْ، هذا بالنسبة للخلق كلهم، أما الخواص من الناس المستثنون من هؤلاء وهم الذين أفاض الله على قلوبهم بأنوار المعارف وحلاهم بحلية الوقار والسكينة، وأنعم عليهم بأنواع اللطائف، وقال: فيما يروى في بعض الأخبار: الإيمان يزيد وينقص، وهذا الإيمان يزيد وينقص، وذلك بتأثير الطاعات في القلب لا يدركه إلا من راقب أحوال نفسه في أوقات المواظبة على العبادة والتجرد لها بحضور القلب مع أوقات الفتور وإدراك التفاوت في السكون إلى عقائد الإيمان في هذه الأحوال حتى يزيد عقده استعصاء على من يريد حله بالتشكيك، بل من يعتقد في اليتيم معنى الرحمة إذا عمل بموجب إعتقاده فمسح رأسه وتلطف به أدرك من باطنه تأكيد الرحمة وتضاعفها بسبب العمل، وكذلك معتقد التواضع إذا عمل بموجبه عملا مقبلاً أو ساجداً لغيره، أحس من قلبه بالتواضع عند إقدامه على الخدمة، وهكذا جميع صفات تصدر منها أعمال الجوارح، ثم يعود دائـر الأعمال عليها فيؤكدها ويزيدها، وسيأتي هذا في ربع المنجيات والمهلكات عند بيان وجه تعلق الباطن بالظاهر، والأعمال بالعقائد والقلوب، فإن ذلك من جنس تعلق الملك بالملكوت، وأعني بالملك القلب.
And this belief is a knot upon the heart; sometimes it becomes strong and firm, and sometimes it becomes weak and loose. Do not consider this far-fetched, and consider it by the Jew and his firmness in his belief, from which he cannot be turned away by intimidation and warning, nor by illusion and preaching, nor by verification and proof; likewise the Christian and the innovators, and among them are those who can be thrown into doubt by the slightest speech, and can be led away from their belief by the least persuasion or intimidation, although he is not doubtful in his knot like the first, but they differ in the strength of determination. And this also exists in true belief. Action influences the growth and increase of this determination, just as watering influences the growth of trees. Therefore the Exalted said: “So it increased them in faith” (Quran 9:124), and He said: “That they may increase in faith upon their faith” (Quran 48:4). This is with respect to all of creation. As for the special ones among people, who are excepted from these, they are those upon whose hearts God has poured illuminations of gnoses, adorned them with the adornment of dignity and tranquility, and bestowed upon them various kinds of subtleties. And he said: According to what is narrated in some reports: “Faith increases and decreases.” And this faith increases and decreases. That is through the effect of acts of obedience upon the heart; none perceives this except one who watches over the states of his soul in times of regular performance of worship and devotion to it with presence of heart, along with times of laxity, and perceives the difference in the tranquility toward the beliefs of faith in these states, until his knot becomes more resistant to one who wants to untie it by casting doubt. Rather, one who believes in the orphan the meaning of mercy, if he acts according to his belief and wipes his head and is gentle with him, he perceives from his inner self the confirmation of mercy and its multiplication due to the action. Likewise, one who believes in humility, if he acts according to it by an action of prostrating or bowing to another, he feels in his heart humility when he undertakes service. And thus all qualities from which the actions of the limbs proceed, then the cycle of actions returns upon them and confirms them and increases them. And this will come in the Quarter of Deliverance and Destruction (Rub‘ al-Munjiyat wal-Muhlikat) when explaining the manner of attachment of the inner to the outer, and actions to beliefs and hearts, for that is of the kind of attachment of the kingdom (mulk) to the dominion (malakut); and by ‘kingdom’ I mean the heart.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a continuous explanation by Imam al-Ghazali about the nature of belief (i‘tiqad) and faith (iman). He begins with an analogy: belief is like a knot (uqdah) on the heart. This knot varies in strength and weakness, which is a known human experience. He illustrates this by pointing to a Jew or Christian who holds firmly to his religion despite attempts to dissuade him, while some innovators can be easily swayed, even though both have a knot of belief. The difference lies in the strength of determination (tasmeem). Ghazali then applies this to true belief (al-i‘tiqad al-haqq), stating that actions affect the growth and increase of this determination, just as watering helps trees grow. He cites Quranic verses that mention increase in faith (ayat 9:124 and 48:4). Next, he distinguishes between ordinary people and the special ones (al-khawass) who have been blessed with divine illuminations and subtleties. Then he mentions a report (hadith) that faith increases and decreases, explaining that this change is due to the effect of acts of obedience on the heart. Only those who observe their own states during worship and times of laxity can perceive this fluctuation. The increased faith makes the knot more resistant to doubt. Ghazali provides concrete examples: if a person believes in mercy toward orphans and acts by wiping the orphan's head, he feels the mercy confirmed and multiplied within. Similarly, acting with humility reinforces that quality. He concludes that all qualities (both praiseworthy and blameworthy) are strengthened by the actions that proceed from them, creating a cycle. He promises further explanation in the Rub‘ al-Munjiyat wal-Muhlikat (The Quarter of Deliverance and Destruction), noting that the connection between inner and outer, and between actions and beliefs, is akin to the relation between the king (mulk) and the dominion (malakut), with the heart being the king.

Key Terms
إعتقاد (i‘tiqad)
عقدة (uqdah)
تصميم (tasmeem)
إيمان (iman)
يزيد وينقص (yazid wa yanqus)
الخواص (al-khawass)
المعرفة (ma‘rifah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith is a static, unchanging quantity.
Correction: Ghazali demonstrates through analogy and examples that faith (the knot) fluctuates in strength based on actions and inner state, directly contradicting the notion of static faith.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali's analogy, what does belief resemble, and what causes it to strengthen?
A) A fortress defended by arguments; it strengthens through debate.
B) A knot on the heart; it strengthens through actions.
C) A tree watered by knowledge; it strengthens through study.
D) A flame fueled by emotion; it strengthens through zeal.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali's analogy teaches that faith is a dynamic knot on the heart, growing tighter through obedient actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you acted on a belief—like showing mercy to an orphan or humbling yourself. Did you feel that belief strengthen inside you? If not, why might your actions have lacked the presence of heart that Ghazali insists on?
?
Which belief in your heart feels most like a loose knot? What specific action (based on Ghazali's examples) could you take today to begin tightening it, and what would 'presence of heart' mean for you in that moment?
?
The lesson says faith increases through actions, but also that we must watch our souls in times of worship and laxity. Are you aware of the difference in your heart between a time of devotion and a time of neglect? What would it take for you to 'perceive' that difference starting tomorrow?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
5 min
Faith increases and decreases through actions of the heart
Ghazali explains the dynamics of faith through action and inner experience.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how faith increases and decreases as a real experiential phenomenon caused by acts of obedience and disobedience, and how inner states are affected by outward actions.

Core Idea
Faith is dynamic: acts of obedience strengthen it in the heart.

Ghazali begins by stating a fundamental principle: faith is not static but increases and decreases. He grounds this in both inner experience and scriptural evidence. In this passage, he invites us to observe our own hearts to perceive how worship strengthens our convictions and slackness weakens them. By reflecting on this, we see the intimate connection between outward actions and inward belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the full translation. Let the author's own argument come through before you interpret.
Notice the flowing style and the use of examples.
2
Identify the experiential insight
Ghazali stresses that the increase is perceived by watching one's own heart during worship versus slackness. Ask yourself: have you ever felt a difference in your faith after consistent worship?
This is a key point: it's not just theoretical.
3
Examine the two examples
Look at the examples of mercy towards an orphan and humility in prostration. See how Ghazali shows that acting on a belief reinforces that belief internally.
These illustrate the cycle of action strengthening inner traits.
4
Note the Quranic evidence
Ghazali cites two Quranic verses showing that fear of enemies and trials increased the believers' faith. This grounds the argument in divine revelation.
This shows the principle is not just experiential but scriptural.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال : فيما يروى في بعض الأخبار : الإيمان يزيد وينقص ، وذلك بتأثير الطاعات في القلب لا يدركه إلا من راقب أحوال نفسه في أوقات المواظبة على العبادة والتجرد لها بحضور القلب مع أوقات الفتور وإدراك التفاوت في السكون إلى عقائد الإيمان في هذه الأحوال حتى يزيد عقده إستعصاء على من يريد حله بالتشكيك بل من يعتقد في اليتيم معنى الرحمة إذا عمل بموجب إعتقاده فمسح رأسه وتلطف به أدرك من باطنه تأكيد الرحمة وتضاعفها بسبب العمل . وكذلك معتقد التواضع إذا عمل بموجبه عملا مقبلاً أو ساجداً لغيره ، أحس من قلبه بالتواضع عند إقدامه على الخدمة وهكذا جميع صفات تصدر منها أعمال الجوارح ، ثم يعود دائـر الأعمال عليها فيؤكدها ويزيدها وسيأتي هذا في ربع المنجيات والمهلكات عند بيان وجه تعلق الباطن بالظاهر، والأعمال بالعقائد والقلوب ، فإن ذلك من جنس تعلق الملك بالملكوت . وفي سورة آل عمران : (فَأَخْشَوْهُمْ فَزَادَهُم إِيمَاناً ) وفي سورة الأحزاب : ﴿ وَمَا زَادَهُمْ إِلَّا إِيمَاناً وَتَسْلِيماً )
And he said: In what is narrated in some reports: Faith increases and decreases, and that is by the effect of acts of obedience in the heart, which none perceives except one who watches his own states during times of perseverance in worship and devoting oneself to it with presence of heart along with times of slackness, and perceives the discrepancy in the tranquility towards the beliefs of faith in these states, until its knot becomes more resistant to one who wishes to undo it by doubt. Rather, one who believes in the meaning of mercy towards an orphan, if he acts according to his belief and wipes his head and treats him kindly, perceives from his inner self the confirmation of mercy and its multiplication due to the action. Similarly, one who believes in humility, if he acts according to his belief by performing an act such as prostrating to another, he feels in his heart humility when he undertakes service. And so all the attributes from which actions of the limbs proceed, then the cycle of actions returns upon them, confirming and increasing them. And this will come in the quarter of the deliverers and the destroyers when clarifying the aspect of connection of the inner with the outer, and actions with beliefs and hearts, for that is of the kind of connection of the kingdom of the visible world with the kingdom of the invisible. And in Surah Al-Imran: 'So they feared them, but it increased them in faith.' And in Surah Al-Ahzab: 'And it only increased them in faith and submission.'
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage defines the increase and decrease of faith as a real experiential phenomenon, not merely metaphorical. Ghazali begins by citing a report that faith increases and decreases, and he explains that this is caused by the effect of acts of obedience on the heart. He stresses that this is only known by one who observes his own states during times of committed worship with presence of heart and times of slackness, perceiving a difference in the tranquility of his beliefs. The stronger the act of worship, the more firmly the knot of faith resists doubt. He then gives two examples: the one who believes in mercy and acts by wiping an orphan's head feels his mercy strengthen internally; similarly, the one who believes in humility and acts by prostrating feels his humility increase. Thus all virtuous traits are reinforced by their corresponding actions. Ghazali then mentions that this topic will be elaborated later in his work, but he immediately supports his claim with Quranic verses from Surah Al-Imran and Surah Al-Ahzab, showing that fear of enemies and trials increased the believers' faith. This passage refutes those who deny the increase and decrease of faith, grounding it in both inner experience and revelation.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think faith is static or that increase is only in knowledge, not in inner conviction.
Correction: Ghazali shows that faith is a real, felt increase in the heart through action, as perceived by self-observation and confirmed by revelation.

A) Recitation of Quran
B) Acts of obedience
C) Debating with doubters
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
Faith increases and decreases as a real inner experience, directly affected by our acts of obedience and disobedience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you noticed your faith feeling stronger or weaker? What specific action—or lack of it—caused that change? Will you now watch your own heart more closely during worship?
?
Think of one attribute like mercy or humility that you believe in but rarely act on. After reading this lesson, can you honestly say you are willing to act on it today, even in a small way, trusting that it will strengthen your faith?
?
You have seen the difference between times of devotion with presence of heart and times of slackness. Do you accept that your neglect in worship is not neutral but actively weakening your faith? What one change will you make this week to reverse that?

Increase of Faith Through Obedience
Ghazali explains how obedience increases faith and cites Ali's statement on the light of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ghazali explains that faith increases through obedience and how the heart transforms accordingly.

Core Idea
Faith grows with obedience; sin blackens the heart until it is sealed.

In this passage, Imam al-Ghazali connects the outer practice of religion (mu'amala) to inner unveiling (mukashafa). He argues that obedience to Allah's commands directly increases faith, visible as a light in the heart. He supports this with a powerful metaphor from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, describing faith as a white spot that expands with good deeds, and hypocrisy as a black spot that spreads with sin. This lesson unpacks the relationship between action and the heart's state.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Ghazali connects the two worlds.
Pay attention to the terms 'mu'amala' and 'mukashafa'.
2
Understand the connection between outer and inner
Ghazali says sciences of unveiling climb upon sciences of dealing. Reflect on how outward obedience leads to inner growth.
This shows that action and faith are linked.
3
Examine the metaphor from 'Ali
Identify the white spot (faith) and black spot (hypocrisy). See how they grow with actions.
The metaphor illustrates the dynamic nature of faith.
4
Relate to the Quranic verse
The phrase 'rust upon hearts' from Surah al-Mutaffifin is quoted. Understand the concept of sealing (khatm).
The seal prevents guidance from entering.
5
Reflect on the lesson
How does this affect your understanding of faith? Is faith static or dynamic?
Consider your own spiritual state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولنرجع إلى المقصود، فإن هذا العالم خارج عن علم المعاملة، ولكن بين العالمين أيضاً إتصال وإرتباط فلذلك ترى علوم المكاشفة تتسلق كل ساعة على علوم المعاملة إلى أن تنكشف عنها بالتكليف فهذا وجه زيادة الإيمان بالطاعة بموجب هذا الإطلاق، ولهذا قال علي كرم الله وجهه، إن الإيمان ليبدو لمعة يضاء، فإذا عمل العبد الصالحات نمت فزادت حتى يبيض القلب كله، وإن النفاق ليبدو نكتة سوداء فإذا إنتهك الحرمات نمت وزادت حتى يسود القلب كله، فيطبع عليه فذلك هو الختم، وتلا قوله تعالى: ﴿ كَلَّا بَلْ رَانَ عَلَى قُلُوبِهِمْ ﴾
Let us return to the purpose: this world is outside the science of dealing (mu'amala), but between the two worlds there is also connection and linkage, so you see the sciences of unveiling (mukashafa) climb every hour upon the sciences of dealing until they are uncovered by obligation. This is the aspect of increase of faith through obedience by virtue of this usage. For this reason 'Ali (may Allah honor his face) said: 'Faith appears as a white spot, and when the servant performs righteous deeds it grows and increases until the whole heart becomes white. And hypocrisy appears as a black spot, and when the sacred limits are violated it grows and increases until the whole heart becomes black, then it is sealed—that is the sealing.' And he recited the words of the Exalted: 'Nay, but that which they have earned has rusted upon their hearts.'
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory argument that connects the earlier discussion of the two worlds to the increase of faith. Ghazali begins by returning to the main subject: the world of shahada and malakut are connected, and the sciences of unveiling (mukashafa) build upon the sciences of outward religious practice (mu'amala). This linkage shows that faith increases through obedience to Allah's commands. He then supports this with a transmission from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, who describes faith as initially a white spot that grows with righteous deeds until the entire heart is white, while hypocrisy starts as a black spot that grows with violations until the heart becomes black and is sealed—this is the 'seal' mentioned in the Quran (Surah al-Mutaffifin, verse 14). Thus, the passage establishes a direct correlation between action and the state of the heart, showing how faith can increase physically (in the heart's purity) through obedience.

Key Terms
علوم المكاشفة
علوم المعاملة
زيادة الإيمان
الختم
الران

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith is static and does not change.
Correction: Faith increases with obedience and decreases with sin; it is dynamic and affected by actions.

Checkpoint

A) A white spot appears on the heart.
B) A black spot appears and grows until the heart becomes black.
C) The heart becomes sealed immediately.
D) The servant loses all faith.

Key Takeaway
Faith is dynamic: it grows with obedience like a white spot expanding until the heart is pure, and diminishes with sin until the heart is sealed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your heart right now, do you see more white spots from your good deeds or black spots from your sins? Which specific sin are you allowing to grow that black spot—and what will you do today to stop feeding it?
?
Ali said righteous deeds make the white spot grow until the whole heart is white. Is there a single righteous deed you have been neglecting that, if you started doing it consistently, would bring light back into your heart? Commit to doing it tonight.
?
The passage warns that even small violations can lead to the entire heart being sealed. Is there a 'small' sin you have been tolerating, thinking it doesn't matter? How will you cut it out of your life starting now, before it rusts your heart?

The Second Meaning of Faith: Belief and Action Together
Ghazali defines the second meaning of faith as both belief and action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali expands the definition of faith to include both inner belief and outward actions, and why this raises the question of whether belief itself can increase or decrease.

Core Idea
Faith includes both belief and action; increase and decrease become visible, but does that change belief itself?

Ghazali has introduced the first meaning of faith as mere belief. Now he turns to a second meaning that incorporates actions. This has profound implications for how we understand the growth or diminishment of faith. The passage presents two hadiths and raises a critical question about the relation between action and the core of belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the two hadiths Ghazali uses to support including actions in faith.
The hadith about seventy-some branches and the hadith about the fornicator are key evidence.
2
Understand the second meaning
Recognize that here faith (iman) means both tasdiq (belief in the heart) and amal (outward actions). This is different from the first meaning where faith was only belief.
With actions included, increase and decrease of faith become apparent through deeds.
3
Ponder the critical question
Ghazali asks whether the increase from actions affects the core of faith, which is mere belief. He says this requires consideration, but indicates that it does affect it. Think about why this question matters for understanding faith.
This connects to the broader debate about whether faith can increase and decrease in essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإطلاق الثاني : أن يراد به التصديق والعمل جميعاً كما قال : « الإيمان بضع وسبعون بابا » وكما قال صلى الله عليه وسلم : « لا يزني الزاني حين يزني وهو مؤمن » وإذا دخل العمل في مقتضى الإيمان لم تخف زيادته ونقصانه ، وهل يؤثر ذلك في زيادة الإيمان الذي هو مجرد التصديق ؟ هذا فيه نظر ، وقد أشرنا إلى أنه يؤثر فيه
The second meaning: that it means both belief (tasdiq) and action (amal) together, as he said: 'Faith has seventy-some branches', and as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The fornicator does not fornicate while he is a believer.' And when action is included in the requirement of faith, its increase and decrease are not hidden. And does that affect the increase of faith which is mere belief? This requires consideration, and we have indicated that it does affect it.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage defines the second meaning of 'increase of faith'. Ghazali presents the view that faith (iman) encompasses both belief (tasdiq) and action (amal). He supports this with two hadiths: one stating faith has seventy-some branches (implying actions are part of faith), and another stating that a fornicator does not fornicate while being a believer (implying that sin negates faith momentarily). He then notes that if action is included in the definition, faith can clearly increase and decrease. However, the key question is whether this increase and decrease affect the core of faith, which is mere belief (tasdiq). He acknowledges that there is room for consideration and mentions that he previously indicated that it does affect it. The passage presents the argument without fully resolving it here.

Key Terms
تصديق
عمل
زيادة
نقصان
إيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that including actions in faith means that the core belief itself changes in a quantitative way, and that this is self-evident without need for consideration.
Correction: Ghazali shows that while including actions makes increase/decrease apparent, whether this affects the core belief (tasdiq) is a matter requiring careful consideration, and he indicates that it does affect it, but it is not a simple straightforward conclusion.

Checkpoint
According to the second meaning, what does faith include?
A) Only belief in the heart
B) Only outward actions
C) Both belief and action
D) Neither belief nor action

Key Takeaway
Ghazali presents a second meaning of faith that includes both belief and action, which makes increase and decrease apparent, and he leaves open the question of whether this affects the core of belief, indicating that it does.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly feel that your faith—not just your actions—has diminished? Or do you comfort yourself by separating what you do from what you believe? Ghazali indicates that action affects belief itself. How does this challenge your own excuses for sin? What will you do today to treat a small sin as a real wound to your iman?
?
If you were to die right now, would you be confident that your belief alone—without your actions—would save you? This lesson suggests that faith in its fullest sense includes action. Where in your daily life do you rely on 'belief-only' faith while neglecting the deeds that Ghazali says are part of iman? Commit to one specific act of obedience today as an expression of your belief.

The Third Meaning of Faith: Certain Belief through Unveiling
Ghazali defines the third meaning of faith as certain belief through unveiling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the third meaning of faith is certain belief through unveiling, and that even absolute certainties vary in the soul's tranquility.

Core Idea
Certain faith is not uniform; its tranquility varies with clarity.

Imam al-Ghazali now presents the highest meaning of faith: certain belief attained through unveiling and direct witnessing. This is the firmest degree of faith, furthest from increase. Yet he adds a subtle insight: even certainties differ in the peace they bring to the soul. Read on to see how he illustrates this with a simple example.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how Ghazali defines this third meaning and then refines it.
2
Understand the key terms

Ghazali contrasts two certainties: 'two is more than one' and 'the world is created'. Why does he say they differ in tranquility? Reflect on how this shows degrees of faith.
This shows that even firm faith can deepen in its peace.

This passage presents the third and highest meaning of faith: certain belief attained through unveiling (kashf) and direct witnessing (mushahada) with the light of inner sight. For example, the certainty that two is more than one is more immediate and tranquil than the certainty that the world is created, even though both are indubitable. This shows that certainty has degrees of clarity and peace. He refers to his earlier discussion in the Book of Knowledge. Finally, he concludes that across all three meanings, the issue of increase in faith is clarified. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the argument is complete for this section.

The Third Sense of Iman: Certainty with Degrees
Ghazali explains the third sense of iman as certain tasdiq and defends its variability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why even the highest level of iman (certain tasdiq) admits increase and decrease, contrary to the assumption that certainty is uniform.

Core Idea
Certainty is not uniform; even yaqin varies in clarity and tranquility.

Ghazali introduces the third sense of iman as certain assent (tasdiq yaqini) attained through spiritual unveiling. This might seem immune to increase, but Ghazali argues that even the highest certainty admits degrees because the soul's tranquility varies with clarity. He supports this with examples and hadith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp Ghazali's argument about the third sense of iman and its variation.
Notice how he transitions from the previous sense to this one.
2
Identify Ghazali's claim about yaqin
Find where Ghazali says certainties differ in clarity and tranquility. What example does he give?
The example of two vs one vs world creation.
3
Understand the hadith evidence
See how Ghazali uses the hadith about different weights of faith to support the variation.
This shows that even in the heart, faith admits different measures.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
How does Ghazali reconcile the third sense with the overall position that iman increases?
He confirms that all senses accept increase.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يزني الزاني حين يزني وهو مؤمن وإذا دخل العمل في مقتضى الإيمان لم تخف زيادته ونقصانه، وهل يؤثر ذلك في زيادة الإيمان الذي هو مجرد التصديق؟ هذا فيه نظر، وقد أشرنا إلى أنه يؤثر فيه. الإطلاق الثالث: أن يراد به التصديق اليقيني على سبيل الكشف وإنشراح الصدر والمشاهدة بنور البصيرة. وهذا أبعد الأقسام عن قبول الزيادة ولكني أقول: الأمر اليقيني الذي لا شك فيه تختلف طمأنينة النفس إليه فليس طمأنينة النفس إلى أن الإثنين أكثر من الواحد كطمأنينتها إلى أن العالم مصنوع حادث وإن كان لا شك في واحد منهما فإن اليقينيات تختلف في درجات الإيضاح، ودرجات طمأنينة النفس إليها. وقد عرضنا لهذه في فضل اليقين من كتاب العلم في باب علماء الآخرة، فلا حاجة إلى الإعادة. وقد ظهر في جميع الإطلاقات أن ما قالوه من زيادة الإيمان ونقصانه حق، وكيف لا وفي الأخبار أن يخرج من النار من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من إيمان. وفي بعض المواضع في خبر آخر: «مثقال دينار» فأي لاختلاف مقاديره إن كان ما في القلب لا يتفاوت؟
The adulterer does not commit adultery while he is a believer. And when action enters into the implication of faith, its increase and decrease are not hidden. Does that affect the increase of faith which is mere tasdiq? This is debatable, and we have indicated that it does affect it. The third sense: that faith is intended as certain tasdiq (tasdiq yaqini) by way of unveiling, expansion of the breast, and witnessing by the light of insight. This is the farthest of the divisions from accepting increase. But I say: The certain matter about which there is no doubt – the soul's tranquility towards it varies. So the soul's tranquility that two is more than one is not like its tranquility that the world is created and originated, though there is no doubt in either. For certainties differ in degrees of clarity and degrees of the soul's tranquility towards them. We have discussed this in the virtue of certainty (yaqin) in the Book of Knowledge in the chapter on the scholars of the afterlife, so there is no need to repeat. And it has become clear in all the senses that what they said about the increase and decrease of faith is true. How could it not be, when in the reports it is stated that one will come out of the Fire who has in his heart a mustard seed's weight of faith, and in another report 'a dinar's weight'? So what accounts for the difference in amounts if what is in the heart does not vary?
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof combined. Ghazali begins by addressing a hadith: the adulterer is not a believer at the moment of adultery, implying that actions affect the status of iman. However, he notes that if iman is mere tasdiq (assent), whether actions increase it is debatable. He then introduces the third sense of iman: certain tasdiq (tasdiq yaqini) attained through unveiling, expansion of the chest, and inner vision. This is the highest level and seems farthest from increase. But Ghazali argues that even this yaqin admits degrees. He gives the example: the certainty that two is more than one is equally certain but the soul's tranquility towards it differs from the certainty that the world is created, even though both are indubitable. Certainties vary in clarity and the soul's tranquility. He refers to his earlier discussion in the Book of Knowledge. Finally, he concludes that all senses of iman accept increase and decrease, as shown by hadith mentioning different weights (mustard seed, dinar) of faith coming out of Hell. The rhetorical question asks: if faith in the heart did not vary, why do the amounts differ? Thus, iman indeed increases and decreases.

تصديق (tasdiq)
يقين (yaqin)
طمأنينة النفس (tuma'nina al-nafs)
زيادة ونقصان (ziyada wa nuqsān)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That yaqin (certainty) is perfectly uniform and cannot vary.
Correction: Ghazali shows that even within certainty, the soul's tranquility differs, so yaqin admits degrees of clarity and tranquility.

Checkpoint

B) It does not increase because it is based on direct vision.
C) It admits increase because even certainty has degrees of clarity and tranquility.
D) It increases only through good deeds, not through certainty.

Key Takeaway
Even the highest certainty of faith admits degrees and can increase, for the soul's tranquility varies with clarity.

?

The Meaning of 'I am a Believer if Allah Wills'
Ghazali justifies the salaf's istithna and refutes an objection about faith's comparability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theological significance of the salaf's use of 'if Allah wills' in expressing faith and why it does not imply doubt but rather acknowledges variation in degrees of faith.

Core Idea
The salaf's 'if Allah wills' does not express doubt but acknowledges the varying degrees of faith among believers.

In this passage, Imam al-Ghazali addresses a common question about the expression 'I am a believer if Allah wills' used by the early Muslims (salaf). Some might think this indicates doubt in one's own faith, but Ghazali explains a deeper theological nuance: faith varies in degree, and the exception (istithna) acknowledges that one's faith is not on par with the prophets and angels. He then defends this position by discussing the nature of certainty and the concept of equivocal quiddity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and the literal translation to get the flow of Ghazali's argument.
Pay attention to the structure: an objection followed by an answer.
2
Identify the objection and answer
The objection is about istithna implying doubt; the answer distinguishes between similitude (mithaliya) and comparison (tashbih).
No one equates the faith of ordinary people with that of prophets.
3
Understand the variation in certainty
Ghazali explains that certainty varies in clarity, not in essence, using the example of the world's origination versus one-half-two.
The speed of conviction differs due to the presence or absence of premises in the mind.
4
Grasp the denial of mushakkik quiddity
Those who deny equivocal quiddity argue that variation is accidental, not part of the essence.
This supports the view that faith is one in essence but differs in degrees accidentally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معنى مسألة: فإن قلت: ما وجه قول السلف: أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله. والإستثناء المثلية تقتضي المساواة في كل الصفات والتشبيه لا يقتضيه فلا أحد يسوي بين إيمان آحاد الناس وإيمان الملائكة والأنبياء يتفاوت بأمور زائدة وقالوا ما يظن من أن القطع يتفاوت قوة إنما هو راجع إلى جلائه وظهوره وإنكشافه، فإذا ظهر القطع بحدوث العالم بعد ترتيب مقدماته المؤدية إليه كان الجزم الكائن فيه كالجزم في حكمنا الواحد نصف الإثنين، وإنما تفاوتهما بإعتبار أنه إذا لوحظ هذا كان سرعة الجزم فيه ليس كالسرعة التي في الآخر وهو الواحد نصف الإثنين خصوصاً مع غيبة النظر عن ترتيب مقدمات حدوث العالم عن الذهن، فيخيل أن الجزم بأن الواحد نصف الاثنين أقوى وليس كذلك، إنما هو أجلى عند العقل فهم ومن وافقهم يمنعون ثبوت ماهية المشكك ويقولون أن الواقع على أشياء متفاوتة فيه يكون التفاوت عارضاً لها خارجاً عنها لا ماهية له ولا جزء ماهية لإمتناع إختلاف الماهية وإختلاف جزئها.
Meaning of the question: If you say: What is the justification for the predecessors' saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills'? And the exception (istithna)? The similitude requires equality in all attributes, but comparison does not require it. So no one equates the faith of ordinary people with the faith of angels and prophets; it varies by additional matters. And they said: What is thought that certainty (qat') varies in strength is only due to its clarity, manifestation, and unveiling. When certainty of the world's origination appears after arranging its premises leading to it, the conviction (jazzm) inherent in it is like the conviction in our judgment that one-half-two [sic], and the difference between them is only considered that if one observes this, the speed of conviction in it is not like the speed in the other, which is that one is half of two, especially with the absence of consideration of the arrangement of the premises of the world's origination from the mind. So one imagines that conviction that one is half of two is stronger, but it is not so; it is only clearer to the intellect. They and those who agree with them deny the existence of a 'mushakkik' (equivocal) quiddity (mahiya) and say that what applies to varying things: the variation is accidental to them, external to them, not part of the quiddity or a part of the quiddity, because the quiddity and its part cannot differ.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. Ghazali poses a question: what is the meaning of the salaf's phrase 'I am a believer if Allah wills' (istithna)? The objection is that if faith is one thing, saying 'if Allah wills' suggests doubt. The answer: The word 'similitude' might imply equality, but 'comparison' (tashbih) does not. No one compares the faith of common people to that of angels and prophets; faith varies by additional matters. They explain that the variation in certainty (qat') is not in its strength per se but in its clarity, manifestation, and unveiling. For example, the certainty that the world is originated (hadith) after arranging premises is not intrinsically weaker than the certainty that one is half of two; the latter appears faster because the premises are not consciously considered. So the difference is in clarity (jala') to the mind, not in the essence of certainty. Those who deny mushakkik quiddity argue that when a concept applies to varying things, the variation is accidental and external, not part of the quiddity or its parts, because the quiddity itself cannot differ.

Key Terms
إستثناء (istithna)
مثلية (mithaliya)
تشبيه (tashbih)
قطع (qat')
جزم (jazzm)
ماهية مشككة (mahiya mushakkika)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The salaf's 'if Allah wills' indicates doubt in one's faith.
Correction: It actually acknowledges the varying degrees of faith, not doubt, and no one equates their faith to that of prophets.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what does the istithna 'if Allah wills' signify in the statement of the salaf?
A) Doubt about one's own faith.
B) Acknowledgment that faith varies in degree among individuals.
C) Fear of hypocrisy.
D) A linguistic convention with no theological meaning.

Key Takeaway
The salaf's istithna does not express doubt but highlights that faith can vary in degree, and certainty (qat') differs in clarity, not in strength.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I am a believer' or 'Masha'Allah', is it ever with a hidden sense of pride in your own faith? How does knowing that the salaf said 'if Allah wills' out of humility (not doubt) challenge you to examine the intentions behind your words? This week, before you speak about your faith, pause and ask Allah to keep you from self-amazement.
?
The passage contrasts certainty that the world is created with certainty that one is half of two. The latter is clearer because its proof is always present. Think of a core Islamic belief you hold—like the existence of God or the truth of the Quran. Is that certainty always clear and present in your mind, or does it fade when you are distracted? What specific steps can you take to make that reality as clear as 2+2=4 in your daily life?
?
Ghazali says variation in faith is accidental, not essential—meaning your faith can increase or decrease in its effects and clarity without changing its true nature. Have you ever felt that your faith has 'left' you during a trial? How does this teaching help you hold onto the hope that the essence of your faith remains, and that you can work on the accidental aspects? Commit to one action today that will bring more clarity to your faith, such as reflecting on a verse of the Quran or making dhikr.

Faith Increases and Decreases: Evidence from Hadith
Imam Ghazali argues that faith can increase and decrease, citing hadith with varying measures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the varying measures of faith in the hadith prove that faith can increase and decrease.

Core Idea
Faith's measures in hadith show it can be more or less.

This passage presents a key proof from the Prophetic hadith that faith is not a fixed quantity. Imam Ghazali argues that if faith were uniform, the different weights mentioned in the reports would be meaningless. The variation in measures demonstrates that faith can be deficient and increase, affirming the doctrine of faith's variability.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the literal translation. Notice the rhetorical question at the end.
The passage is concise but packed with meaning.
2
Identify the two hadith measures
The passage mentions two measures: a grain-weight and a dinar-weight. Understand what each represents in terms of magnitude.
A grain is very small, a dinar is larger.
3
Understand the logical inference
Ghazali asks: if faith never varies, why would the hadith specify different amounts? The difference implies variation.
This is a simple but powerful argument.
4
Reflect on the doctrinal significance
Consider why this matters: if faith can increase and decrease, then believers must strive to increase it through worship and good deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان ونقصانه حق ، وكيف لا وفي الأخبار أن يخرج من النار من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من إيمان. وفي بعض المواضع في خبر آخر مثقال دينار فأي لاختلاف مقاديره إن كان ما في القلب لا يتفاوت؟
Faith and its deficiency are true. How could it not be, when in the reports (there is) that he will come out of the Fire who has in his heart a grain-weight of faith? And in some places in another report, 'a dinar-weight'. So what is the meaning of the difference in its measures if what is in the heart does not vary?
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the position that faith can increase and decrease. Imam Ghazali states that faith and its deficiency are real (not just metaphorical). He asks rhetorically how could it not be, given the hadith reports that a person will exit the Fire if they have even a grain-weight of faith in their heart. Another report mentions a dinar-weight. The variation in the measures (grain vs. dinar) indicates that the amount of faith in the heart is not uniform. If faith were invariable, the difference in measures would be meaningless. Thus, the evidence from the differing hadith proves that faith can vary.

نقصان
مثقال ذرة
مثقال دينار
تفاوت

Misconception: Faith is a single indivisible entity that cannot vary.
Correction: The hadith mention different weights (grain vs. dinar), indicating that faith can be more or less, not simply present or absent.

B) That faith can vary in amount.

D) That the reports are contradictory.

Key Takeaway
The varying measures of faith in the hadith demonstrate that faith is not a fixed quantity but can increase and decrease.

Defending the Exception Phrase in Declaring Faith
Ghazali explains and defends the salaf's use of 'in sha Allah' in declaring faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the salaf used the phrase 'in sha Allah' when declaring faith, and how Ghazali defends this practice against the objection that it implies doubt.

Core Idea
Faith is certain, but its degrees vary; 'in sha Allah' acknowledges that true reality is known to God.

When the righteous predecessors (salaf) said 'I am a believer, if God wills,' some critics argued that this exception implies doubt. Yet the salaf were not uncertain about their faith; they were acknowledging that faith can increase and decrease. In this passage, Ghazali explains the deeper rationale, using the analogy of certainty and the nature of essence to show that the exception is valid and does not undermine faith's certainty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Ghazali uses a very compressed argument here.
2
Identify the objection
The passage opens with an objection: what is the meaning of the salaf saying 'I am a believer, if God wills'? The objector thinks the exception (istithna) implies doubt or comparison that requires equality.
Understand why using 'if God wills' might be seen as problematic.
3
Understand the first part of the answer
Ghazali responds that faith varies in strength (fada'il), so no one equates the faith of common people with that of prophets and angels. The exception acknowledges this variation, not doubt.
The exception is about degrees, not certainty.
4
Follow the analogy with certainty
Ghazali uses the example of certainty about the world's temporality (huduth al-'alam) and certainty that one is half of two. Both are certain, but one appears clearer due to mental accessibility. The difference is in clarity, not in the essence of certainty.
This analogy shows that something can be certain yet vary in apparent strength.
5
Reflect on the philosophical principle
Those who deny 'mushtarak' essence argue that difference in attributes does not affect the essence. This supports the view that faith's essence is one, and the exception refers to accidental qualities.
This is a deeper linguistic and metaphysical justification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت . ما وجه قول السلف : أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله . والإستثناء المثلية تقتضي المساواة في كل الصفات والتشبيه لا يقتضيه فلا أحد يسوي بين إيمان آحاد الناس وإيمان الملائكة والأنبياء يتفاوت بأمور زائدة وقالوا ما يظن من أن القطع يتفاوت قوة إنما هو راجع إلى جلائه وظهوره وإنكشافه ، فإذا ظهر القطع بحدوث العالم بعد ترتيب مقدماته المؤدية إليه كان الجزم الكائن فيه كالجزم في حكمنا الواحد نصف الإثنين ، وإنما تفاوتهما بإعتبار أنه إذا لوحظ هذا كان سرعة الجزم فيه ليس كالسرعة التي في الآخر وهو الواحد نصف الإثنين خصوصاً مع غيبة النظر عن ترتيب مقدمات حدوث العالم عن الذهن ، فيخيل أن الجزم بأن الواحد نصف الاثنين أقوى وليس كذلك ، إنما هو أجلى عند العقل فهم ومن وافقهم يمنعون ثبوت ماهية المشكك ويقولون أن الواقع على أشياء متفاوتة فيه يكون التفاوت عارضاً لها خارجاً عنها لا ماهية له ولا جزء ماهية لإمتناع إختلاف الماهية وإختلاف جزئها .
If you say: What is the meaning of the statement of the Salaf, 'I am a believer, if God wills'? The exception for comparison requires equality in all attributes, and likeness does not require it, so no one equates the faith of common people with that of angels and prophets, for it varies by additional matters. And they said: What is thought that certainty differs in strength is only due to its clarity, appearance, and disclosure. For when certainty about the temporality of the world appears after arranging its premises leading to it, the conviction therein is like conviction in our judgment that one is half of two. Their difference is only in that when this is observed, the speed of conviction in it is not like the speed in the other, namely that one is half of two, especially when the mind is absent from the arrangement of the premises of the world's temporality. So it is imagined that the conviction that one is half of two is stronger, but it is not so; it is only clearer to the intellect. Those who agree with them deny the existence of a 'mushtarak' essence and say that what applies to different things, the difference is accidental to them, external to them, and is neither the essence nor a part of the essence, because it is impossible for the essence and its part to differ.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer regarding the salaf's practice of saying 'I am a believer, if God wills'. The objector questions how the exception can be valid when it might imply doubt. Ghazali explains that the salaf did not intend doubt; rather, they meant that faith varies in degrees and its ultimate reality is known only to God. The comparison of faith to certainty (qat') is used: certainty about the world's temporality and certainty that one is half of two are both certain, but they differ in clarity and speed of conviction. The difference is not in the essence of certainty but in external factors like clarity. Those who deny 'mushtarak' (equivocal) essences hold that when a term applies to different things, the difference is accidental, not part of the essence. Thus, faith's essence is one, but its degrees vary by accidental qualities.

Key Terms
الإستثناء
السلف
القطع
الجزم
الماهية المشكك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that saying 'I am a believer, if God wills' indicates doubt in one's own faith.
Correction: The salaf used this phrase to acknowledge that faith varies in strength and its ultimate state is known only to God. It does not undermine the certainty of faith; it reflects humility and reliance on God.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, why did the salaf say 'I am a believer, if God wills'?
A) Because they doubted their own faith.
B) Because they were not certain about the future of their faith.
C) Because faith varies in strength and only God knows its ultimate reality.
D) Because they were required to do so by a hadith.

Key Takeaway
The salaf's use of 'in sha Allah' in declaring faith does not imply doubt but acknowledges that faith's degrees are known only to God, and the essence of faith remains one.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'in shā' Allāh' about your faith, do you genuinely acknowledge that your certainty is variable? Or do you use it as a mere formality? What would change if you meant it deeply?
?
If the essence of faith is one but degrees vary, how does that challenge your evaluation of others' faith—especially those whose practice or conviction seems weaker than yours?
?
Ghazali says certainty does not differ in strength, only in clarity. Think of a moment when you felt your faith was 'stronger'—was it actually clearer due to reflection? What practical step can you take today to increase that clarity?

Doubt in Faith is Disbelief: The Position of Sufyan al-Thawri
Ghazali condemns doubt in faith and presents Sufyan al-Thawri's strict view on declaring faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why doubt in faith is considered disbelief according to Ghazali and how Sufyan al-Thawri's strict view on declaring faith offers a cautious path.

Core Idea
Doubt in faith is disbelief; yet even certainty must be expressed with humility.

This passage tackles a delicate issue: how should a believer declare their faith? Ghazali begins by ruling that doubting one's faith is outright disbelief. He then presents the position of the eminent scholar Sufyan al-Thawri, who warns against both overconfidence and innovation in declaring faith. As we read, we'll explore the reasoning behind this caution and its resolution in Quranic language.

Guided Path
1
Understand the prohibition of doubt
Read the opening sentence where Ghazali states that doubt in faith is disbelief. This sets the absolute boundary.
2
Examine Sufyan's two statements
Notice how Sufyan condemns two ways of declaring faith: saying 'I am a believer with God' as a lie, and 'I am a believer in myself' as an innovation.
The commentary will explain the rationale.
3
Reason through the animal analogy
Read the analogy: if asked 'Are you an animal?', one cannot say 'I am an animal if God wills'. This shows that some self-knowledge is certain and does not require exception.
4
Learn the recommended response
See how Sufyan resolves the issue by quoting the Quran: 'We believe in God and what has been sent down to us.' This shifts focus to objective declaration.
This is the takeaway for practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شك (١) ، والشك في الإيمان كفر ، وقد كانوا يمتنعون عن جزم الجواب بالإيمان ويحترزون عنه : فقال سفيان الثوري رحمه الله من قال أنا مؤمن عند الله فهو من الكاذبين ومن قال أنا مؤمن في نفسه فهو بدعة ، فكيف يكون كاذباً وهو يعلم أنه كان مؤمناً في نفسه كان مؤمناً عند الله ومن وسخياً في نفسه وعلم ذلك كان كذلك عند الله ، وكذا من مسروراً ، أو حزيناً ، أو سميعاً أو بصيراً . ولو قيل للإنسان . هل أنت حيوان لم يحسن أن يقول أنا حيوان إن شاء الله ولما قال سفيان ذلك قيل له : فماذا نقول ؟ قال : قُولُوا آمَنَّا بِاللَّهِ وَمَا أُنزِلَ إِلَيْنَا .
Doubt, and doubt in faith is disbelief. And they used to refrain from giving a definitive answer about faith and were cautious about it. So Sufyan al-Thawri, may God have mercy on him, said: 'He who says, "I am a believer with God," is among the liars. And he who says, "I am a believer in myself," it is an innovation.' So how can he be a liar while he knows that he was a believer in himself, he was a believer with God, and whoever is miserly in himself and knows that, he is likewise with God. And similarly, one who is joyful, or sad, or hearing, or seeing. And if it were said to a person, 'Are you an animal?' it would not be proper for him to say, 'I am an animal if God wills.' And when Sufyan said that, it was said to him, 'So what should we say?' He said: 'Say: We believe in God and what has been sent down to us.'
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal ruling on doubt in faith and the proper way to affirm it. Ghazali begins by stating that doubt in faith is disbelief. The early Muslims avoided giving an unqualified affirmation of faith out of caution. He then quotes Sufyan al-Thawri: One who says 'I am a believer with God' is lying, because true knowledge of one's faith belongs to God. Saying 'I am a believer in myself' is an innovation (bid'a). The reasoning is that if one knows he is a believer in himself, then he is indeed a believer with God, so the exception is unnecessary. To illustrate, if asked 'Are you an animal?', one would not say 'I am an animal if God wills' because it is inherently known. When asked what to say instead, Sufyan instructs to quote the verse: 'We believe in God and what has been sent down to us' (Quran 2:136). This shifts the focus from subjective self-assessment to objective declaration of faith.

Key Terms
شك
كفر
سفيان الثوري
جزم
بدعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that avoiding a definitive statement about faith means that doubt is permissible or that one cannot be certain of being a believer.
Correction: The caution is about claiming knowledge of God's final judgment, not about the truth of faith itself. One can be certain of one's own belief but should not assert that God has accepted it.

Checkpoint
According to Sufyan al-Thawri, what is the ruling on saying 'I am a believer with God'?
A) It is recommended.
B) It is a lie.
C) It is an innovation.
D) It is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Faith must be affirmed with certainty, but when declaring it, we should avoid claiming knowledge of God's judgment and instead use the Quranic phrase 'We believe in God and what has been sent down to us.'

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you affirm your faith, do you do so with the implicit assumption that you know God's final judgment of you? How does this lesson challenge that assumption, and what will you change about how you speak of your faith starting today?
?
Are there areas of doubt in your heart about your religion that you have ignored, thinking they are minor or harmless? What does the opening statement 'doubt in faith is disbelief' demand of you right now?
?
If you were asked to declare your faith publicly, would your answer reflect the caution of the salaf or a careless certainty? What step will you take to ensure your words align with the Quranic response taught here?

The Use of 'إن شاء الله' in Relation to Iman: Doubt in Its Perfection, Not Its Foundation
Ghazali clarifies the meaning of 'إن شاء الله' after declaring faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that saying 'أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله' expresses doubt about the perfection of one's faith, not its foundation, and that this is not disbelief.

Core Idea
'إن شاء الله' after declaring faith shows humility about perfection, not doubt in truth.

Imam Ghazali now addresses a common practice: Muslims sometimes say 'أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله' (I am a believer, if Allah wills). This might seem to imply uncertainty about one's faith itself. But Ghazali clarifies that this is not doubt in the fundamentals of Islam; rather, it is an acknowledgment that one's faith may not be at its highest level. This distinction is crucial for avoiding misunderstandings about the nature of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note how Ghazali distinguishes between doubt in the foundation and doubt in perfection.
2
Understand the Quranic reference
Ghazali cites Quran 8:4 which describes some as 'believers truly'. Reflect on why this verse supports the idea of degrees of faith.
3
Identify the two categories
The passage mentions two divisions regarding doubt in perfection: those who are truly believers and those who are not. Think about how this applies to every Muslim.
4
Grasp the consensus
Ghazali states that only doubt in the foundation is kufr by consensus. Confirm that this aligns with mainstream Islamic theology.
5
Apply the insight
Consider how this teaching affects the way you view your own faith and how you should think about others' faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثالث: مستندة الشك، ومعناه: أنا مؤمن حقاً إن شاء الله، إذ قال الله تعالى لقوم مخصوصين بأعيانهم: أُوْلَئِكَ هُمُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ حَقًّا. فانقسموا إلى هذا إلى الشك في كمال الإيمان لا في أصله، وكل إنسان يرجع شاكاً في كمال إيمانه، وذلك ليس بكفر، والشك في كمال الإيمان حق من قسمين: قسم يطلق عليهم أنهم مؤمنون حقاً، وقسم لا يطلق عليهم ذلك. وليس الكفر الشك في الإيمان، وإنما الموسوم بالكفر هو الشك في أصله وثبوته للحال بالإتفاق.
The third aspect: It is based on doubt, and its meaning is: 'I am truly a believer if Allah wills,' since Allah, exalted, said to a particular people by their very selves: 'Those are the believers truly.' So they are divided by this into doubt about the perfection of faith, not its foundation. Every person returns doubtful about the perfection of his faith, and that is not disbelief. And doubt in the perfection of faith is correct from two divisions: a division of whom it is said that they are truly believers, and a division of whom that is not said. And disbelief is not doubt in faith; rather, what is marked as disbelief is doubt in its foundation and its present state by scholarly consensus.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage deals with the third usage: using 'إن شاء الله' when claiming to be a believer (e.g., 'أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله'). The author clarifies that this does not indicate doubt about the existence of Allah or the truth of Islam, but doubt about the perfection of one's faith. The Quranic verse (8:4) distinguishes true believers from others, implying degrees. Every Muslim should be uncertain about whether they have attained that complete level. This doubt is not kufr; only doubting the foundation of faith is kufr. The author also divides people into two categories: those who are truly believers (the ones described in the verse) and those who are not. Consensus supports this distinction.

Key Terms
إيمان
كمال
شك
كفر
حق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Saying 'أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله' implies disbelief or doubt in Allah's existence
Correction: The phrase indicates doubt in the perfection of one's faith, not its foundation. Doubting the foundation is kufr, but doubting perfection is not.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what kind of doubt is expressed by saying 'أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله'?
A) Doubt in Allah's existence
B) Doubt in the perfection of one's faith
C) Doubt in the truth of Islam
D) Doubt in the Prophet's mission

Key Takeaway
Saying 'أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله' is an expression of humility about one's level of faith, not a denial of faith itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله', do you truly intend humility about your faith's perfection, or do you say it as a mere habit without reflection? How can you make this expression more sincere?
?
How often do you examine your own faith to see if it meets the standard of the 'true believers' described in the Quran? Are you content with being a generic Muslim, or do you strive for the perfection that Ghazali speaks of?
?
Is there a part of your heart that fears that doubting your faith's perfection might somehow weaken it? What would it take for you to embrace the humility of saying 'إن شاء الله' without feeling defensive?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate

The Third Face: Doubt in Perfection of Faith
Ghazali defines the third face regarding the statement 'I am a believer if Allah wills'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between doubt in the foundation of faith and doubt in its perfection, and why the expression 'if Allah wills' can signify seeking blessing and politeness rather than genuine uncertainty.

Core Idea
Doubt in the perfection of faith is not disbelief; it is a sign of humility.

In this passage, Ghazali addresses a subtle issue regarding the statement 'I am a believer if Allah wills.' Some might think that saying 'if Allah wills' indicates doubt in one's faith. Ghazali explains that the doubt here concerns the perfection of faith, not its foundation. He further clarifies that the phrase can be used for seeking blessing (tabarruk) and politeness (ta'adub), as demonstrated by the hadith of Prophet Solomon.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the structure: Ghazali first defines the third face, then explains the doubt is in perfection, then introduces an alternative meaning for 'if Allah wills'.
Pay attention to the key terms like 'kamaal' and 'asl'.
2
Identify the key distinction
Identify the two categories: doubt in the foundation of faith (asl) vs. doubt in its perfection (kamaal). Understand that Ghazali says doubt in perfection is not disbelief.
3
Reflect on the hadith evidence
Read the hadith about Prophet Solomon. Consider how the omission of 'if Allah wills' led to a lack of blessing. This illustrates the alternative meaning of tabarruk and ta'adub.
The hadith is cited to support the idea that saying 'if Allah wills' is a form of seeking blessing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثالث : مستندة الشك ، ومعناه : أنا مؤمن حقاً إن شاء الله (۲) إذ قال الله تعالى لقوم مخصوصين بأعيانهم : ( أُوْلَئِكَ هُمُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ حَقًّا ) (۳). فانقسموا إلى هذا إلى الشك في كمال الإيمان لا في أصله ، وكل إنسان ويرجع شاك في كمال إيمانه ، وذلك ليس بكفر (٥) ، والشك في كمال الإيمان حق من قسمين وجهين : (٤) (۱) وحاصل هذا الوجه إنهم خرجوا إن شاء الله ههنا إلى معنى آخر غير الشك وهو التبرك والتأدب وإستدل عليه بالآيتين ، وحديث المقابر ومن أحسن ما يستشهد به هنا ما أخرجه البخاري عن أبي اليمان عن شعيب عن أبي الزناد عن الأعرج عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه أنه سمع النبي قال : قال سليمان عليه السلام لأطوفن الليلة على تسعين إمرأة كلهن تأتي بفارس يجاهد في سبيل فلم يقل إن شاء الله ، فطاف عليهن جميعاً ، فلم تحمل منهن إلا إمرأة واحدة جاءت بشق رجل والذي نفس محمد بيده ، لو قال إن شاء الله لجاهدوا في سبيل الله فرساناً أجمعون الله ، قال له صاحبه : إن شاء الله
The third face: it is based on doubt, and its meaning: I am a true believer if Allah wills (2) when Allah said to a people specifically designated: 'Those are the believers truly' (3). So they are divided into this: doubt in the perfection of faith, not in its origin, and every person returns doubting the perfection of his faith, and that is not disbelief (5), and doubt in the perfection of faith is true from two divisions and two faces: (4) (1) The summary of this face is that they took 'if Allah wills' here to another meaning other than doubt, and it is seeking blessing and politeness, and they adduced evidence for it with the two verses and the hadith of graves. Among the best evidence cited here is what al-Bukhari narrated from Abu al-Yaman from Shu'ayb from Abu al-Zinad from al-A'raj from Abu Hurayra (may Allah be pleased with him) that he heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) say: Solomon (peace be upon him) said: 'I will surely go around tonight to ninety women, each of them will come with a horseman who fights in the path of Allah,' and he did not say 'if Allah wills.' So he went around to all of them, and none of them became pregnant except one woman who came with half a man. By the One in whose hand is the soul of Muhammad, if he had said 'if Allah wills,' they would have all fought as horsemen in the path of Allah. His companion said to him: 'if Allah wills.'
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage defines the third face (wajh) concerning the statement 'I am a true believer if Allah wills.' It clarifies that the doubt expressed by 'if Allah wills' pertains to the perfection (kamaal) of one's faith, not to its foundation (asl). The author states that every person is doubtful about the perfection of his faith, and that this doubt is not disbelief (kufr). Then he explains that the phrase 'if Allah wills' in this context is not actually expressing doubt but is used for seeking blessing (tabarruk) and politeness (ta'adub). He supports this with the hadith of Solomon (AS), who neglected to say 'if Allah wills' and thus only one woman out of ninety became pregnant with a half-child. The lesson emphasizes that the doubt is about the completeness of iman, not its validity, and that such doubt is permissible.

Key Terms
شك
كمال الإيمان
أصل الإيمان
تبرك
تأدب
استثناء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that any doubt in faith is disbelief.
Correction: This passage shows that doubt in the perfection of faith is not disbelief; it is a permissible expression of humility.

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the meaning of 'if Allah wills' when used in the statement 'I am a true believer if Allah wills'?
A) It expresses doubt about the foundation of faith.
B) It expresses doubt about the perfection of faith and is not disbelief.
C) It is a sign of hypocrisy.
D) It is obligatory to say it.

Key Takeaway
Doubt in the perfection of faith is not disbelief; it can be an expression of humility and seeking Allah's blessing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think about a moment when you felt your faith was perfect. Was that feeling genuine or prideful? Now, consider: if you truly believe that only Allah can grant perfection, why do you not constantly say 'if Allah wills'? Will you commit to using this phrase as a sincere plea for perfection, not just a habit?
?
If you were asked today, 'Are you a true believer?' how would you answer? Would your answer reveal a hidden pride or a humble acknowledgment of your shortcomings? What would it cost you to admit that your faith is not yet perfect?
?
Read the hadith of Solomon again. He omitted 'if Allah wills' and suffered loss. In your daily life, where are you acting as if your success is guaranteed by your own efforts? Will you begin to attach 'if Allah wills' to every planned action, trusting that Allah's will is what brings completion?
